Current Affairs Commentary

Brewing of the International Peace Conference

— Star

U.S. President Roosevelt will personally attend the Pan-American Peace Conference in South America next month. In its nature, as the editorial said yesterday, this conference contains the implication of a new Monroe Doctrine. However, from another perspective, it can also be said that this is Roosevelt's first step towards working for international peace. According to Washington dispatches, Roosevelt is now preparing to convene an international conference to discuss ways to maintain peace. Regardless of whether this move can be realized, there is no doubt that Roosevelt wants to do his best for world peace. The Washington Naval Treaty is about to expire, there is no hope for the establishment of a new Locarno Treaty in Europe, and the power of the League of Nations has reached its lowest point. If Roosevelt takes the lead in international peace with the prestige of his election victory, it will certainly be an exciting and meaningful thing.

Is it possible to convene the "International Peace Conference"? Pessimists believe that American presidents often only talk but have no practical action. President Wilson put forward the ideal of the League of Nations, and the whole world followed his lead. After the League of Nations was signed, the United States temporarily refused to ratify it. In 1933, Roosevelt also actively advocated holding an international economic conference. After the conference was held in London, he temporarily changed his mind and refused to stabilize currency prices and reduce tariffs. Similarly, President Coolidge proposed the Kellogg-Briand Pact, and President Hoover proposed the Stimson Doctrine, refusing to recognize "Manchukuo." On the surface, they all sounded very good, but in reality, they rarely benefited peace. Therefore, even if President Roosevelt advocates convening an international peace conference now, how much practical effect it will have is still a question.

Judging from the past and present situation, the future of American peace diplomacy does indeed have great obstacles. However, we must also admit that Roosevelt's current position is at least different from that of Wilson in 1920, Coolidge in 1927, and Hoover in 1931. The biggest reason why American presidents cannot work hard for world peace lies in the constraints of the Senate. The establishment of a treaty requires a two-thirds majority vote in the Senate. Wilson's failure was due to the opposition of the Senate. Now, Roosevelt has the ability to absolutely control the Senate. In this election, the Democratic Party won 75 seats in the Senate, and the Republican Party only had 17 seats. The election of Democratic senators was mostly the result of Roosevelt's help. Therefore, Congress will not oppose any international agreement signed by Roosevelt. The failure of the London Economic Conference was because Roosevelt could not control the economic forces of various factions in the country at that time, so his proposals were uncertain. Now his foreign trade policy has become very concrete. He advocates reducing tariffs and stabilizing currency prices to promote international trade. The recent monetary agreement between the United States, Britain, and France, and the reciprocal tariff agreements between the United States and various European and American countries, all indicate the consistency of this policy. The situation in 1936 cannot be compared with that in 1933.

As for the nominal diplomacy of Hoover and the empty diplomacy of Coolidge, there are many reasons. Most of these reasons no longer exist. The personal leadership of Hoover and Coolidge was very low. Their personalities were far less great than those of Wilson and Roosevelt. Their political skills were also not as strong as theirs. During the Hoover era, the United States' preparedness in the Far East was insufficient. Therefore, its protest against Japan was only in writing and not in fact. After four years of actively increasing military preparations, the United States' voice in the Far East has increased a lot, because force is often the most effective backing for diplomacy. If Stimson were in today's situation, he would be able to do more than he did in 1931. Roosevelt is not an idealist like Wilson. He is very practical. He may be able to make good use of the United States' superior position in military and financial strength to save international peace from the crisis of war.

Of course, we cannot be too optimistic, because the world's aggressive forces are now uniting and trying to undermine peace in various ways. The Washington Treaty system, the Locarno Treaty system, and the League of Nations system have all been destroyed. It takes great effort, great statesmen, and strong determination to rebuild world or regional collective peace. However, in the current international situation, which is at a critical moment, it is the time when "the hungry are easy to feed and the thirsty are easy to drink." We hope that the "International Peace Conference" will become a reality from an ideal, and we hope that this conference will have at least the same success as the Washington Conference of 1922 on the Far East issue.

The Vigor of American Revival, Unprecedented Prosperity in All Industries, Increased Wages and Greatly Reduced Unemployment, Roosevelt Opens the World's Largest Bridge

(New York) The song "Happy Days Are Here Again" sung by the Roosevelt government is gradually being realized. At present, American commerce has gradually become prosperous, and its prosperity is unprecedented. The cost of living has risen quite high. Wages in industries such as steel, automobiles, paper, and clothing have increased by 10% to 20%. Postmaster General Farley predicts that the number of gifts purchased by people before Christmas this year will be the largest in American history. The number of unemployed has decreased from a peak of 15 million in 1933 to less than 9 million. The total amount of wages paid nationwide is the highest since 1930. The gross income of farmers this year is approximately $7,850,000,000. President Roosevelt's determination to balance the budget and stabilize tax rates has had a positive impact on the stock market. Various businesses are now issuing dividends and stocks one after another. (Reuters, 12th)

San Francisco President Roosevelt pressed a gold button in the White House today, and the world's largest bridge newly built in the East Port here immediately lit up with green lights, opening to traffic. At that time, several airplanes circled in the sky, and more than a dozen warships were stationed nearby. About 200,000 people gathered at the bridgehead to watch. Within two and a half hours after the new bridge was opened, more than 16,000 vehicles passed through. The toll collected per hour reached $4,000. If calculated at this speed, all the bridge construction costs can be recovered with interest within 770 days, instead of the 20 years estimated by financiers. This bridge has been planned for a hundred years, and this dream has now been realized. Therefore, people here will celebrate wildly for four days. The bridge construction project lasted for two years. The groundbreaking ceremony was held in mid-February 1933. The bridge is more than eight miles long and can be called the only large bridge in the world. It starts from San Francisco, crosses Yerba Buena Island, and reaches Oakland. The bridge pillars are 519 feet high and 235 feet deep in the water. The bridge cables are 28 inches in diameter. (National News Agency, 12th)

San Francisco The Governor of California, Merriam, cut the golden chain on the bridge, and thousands of cars immediately drove across the bridge. The bridge is eight and a quarter miles long and cost 90 million US dollars. Construction began on July 9, 1933, and was completed last month. The cost was shared by California and the Reconstruction Finance Corporation, which purchased 62 million dollars in bonds. 6,000 people worked directly on the project. It is estimated that the toll revenue collected in the next 20 years can repay the construction costs. The bridge has two suspension sections, each 2,310 feet long, and two two-story tunnels, 540 feet long and 63 feet wide, that run through Yerba Buena Island in the middle of the bay to connect the two parts of the bridge. (Reuters, 12th)

World Peace Depends on Pacific Peace, Britain, America, and Australia Should Cooperate

San Francisco Captain Dudley, a director of the Australian Bank and former technical director of the British Hanterley Peach Airplane Company, has been in contact with the British War Office for a year. He passed through here today on his return to Australia and said that world peace depends on peace in the Pacific. Peace in the Pacific depends on whether Britain, America, and Australia can quickly complete air defense and air routes. There is an absolute need to open up aviation between the United States, Australia, and New Zealand. The future of the Pacific is in the hands of the three countries. The three countries should jointly complete the defense of the Pacific. The time is now. European wars can break out at any time. Britain, America, and Australia should form an English-speaking group to protect peace in the Pacific and let Europe handle its own problems. Dudley expressed satisfaction with the development of the aviation industry in the Pacific. He said that in addition to the Pacific route operated by United Airlines and the aviation lines connecting Australian, London, and European capitals by British Imperial Airways and Dutch Airlines, there are at least two major trunk lines under consideration. One line will be opened by Britain, from Honolulu to Brisbane, and the other will be opened by the United States, from Honolulu to New Zealand, and then extended from New Zealand to Australia. This section will probably be opened by an Australian company. Dudley finally said that this aviation line is actually the basis for strengthening air defense in the Pacific. (National News Agency, 12th)

Britain Builds New Barracks in Kowloon, Can Accommodate 3,000 Soldiers

(London) The Financial Secretary of the War Office, Mr. Warrender, gave a detailed account of the new barracks in Kowloon in response to questions in the House of Commons today. He said that the barracks can accommodate 2,700 British soldiers and 900 Indian soldiers. The larger one can be completed by the end of 1940. The cost is £1.35 million. The barracks must be able to accommodate the increased troops and the defense forces currently living in temporary huts. (Reuters, 12th)

Tense German-Russian Relations, Russian Arrest of Foreign Nationals is a Prelude to a Major Case, Denies Secret Police Assassinated Stalin

(Berlin) Since the German ambassador to Russia, following government instructions, lodged a serious protest with the Soviet Union against the Soviet Union's arrest of five German nationals on charges of espionage and anti-Russian activities, the situation between Russia and Germany has become increasingly tense. According to news from the official German news agency, the five Germans arrested by the Soviet Union were completely innocent. Among them were music teachers, bookkeepers, and mechanics. The news agency's Moscow correspondent said that many Russians arrested at the same time as the Germans were related to the German embassy. Some were staff members of German schools or German Evangelical churches. According to a certain newspaper of the National Socialist Party, the chief of the Soviet secret police, Soskovsky, has been executed by shooting for allegedly plotting to assassinate Stalin. Soskovsky was the head of the Polish Department of the Soviet Secret Police. (Reuters, 13th)

(Berlin) It is reported that in addition to the five Germans, there are also two British, nine Polish, and two Swiss nationals who have been arrested in Moscow. Some of them were going to Moscow to participate in the celebration of the "October Revolution." It is unfortunate that they have now been arrested. However, according to the Soviet police, their purpose in coming to Russia this time was only to contact Trotskyite followers inside and outside the Soviet Union. (Reuters, 13th)

(Berlin) Among the arrested German nationals are Mr. Semmig, the leader of the Moscow branch of the German Dalisten Trading Company, and Mr. Leitz, the director of the Lisbon branch, which has left the branch company unmanaged. Many believe that this arrest storm is a prelude to a major case, which will still be prosecuted by Vyshinsky, the prosecutor in the famous Zinoviev and other counter-revolutionary cases. Today, various newspapers here have criticized the Soviet Union. The Berlin Daily News stated that in view of the Soviet Union's large-scale arrest of foreign nationals, it is almost entirely directed at the German people, and Germany should pay special attention to it. (Reuters, 13th)

Warsaw It is reported that more than 100 people have been arrested in Moscow for discovering a conspiracy to establish a fascist organization in Russia. (Reuters, 13th)

(Moscow) According to official sources, there are no British nationals among the foreign nationals arrested in the Soviet Union. (Reuters, 13th)

(Moscow) Today, the Soviet authorities denied the news from Berlin that Soskovsky, the leader of the Soviet secret police, had been executed by shooting for allegedly plotting to assassinate Stalin. It is said that "the name Soskovsky is very common in Russia, and there is no such name among the key figures in the secret police. (Reuters, 13th)

Japanese Embassy in Poland Decides to Upgrade, Delicate Relations with Germany

(Tokyo) As a result of the meeting of bureau and section chiefs held by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on the 13th, a request was made to the Ministry of Finance to increase the budget for the next year by 2 to 3 million yuan. Now, as a result of the budget review, it has been decided to upgrade the embassy in Poland to an embassy. It is said that the reason is that Poland has delicate diplomatic relations with Russia and Germany, and occupies an important position in diplomacy, so this move has been taken. In addition, the development of Japanese trade and commerce in various parts of the South Seas is of great importance. Therefore, new consulates have been established in several places in the South Seas. In addition, there is the establishment of an etiquette officer in the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate various matters with foreign envoys stationed in Japan or exchange information. (Domei News Agency, 13th)

International Labor Organization Forms Standing Committee, Meeting in Asia

(Geneva) At the International Labor Conference, a resolution proposed by the labor representatives of India and Japan was passed in June this year, advocating the establishment of a standing committee to specialize in studying labor issues in Asian countries, and suggesting convening a labor conference of Asian countries. The Governing Body of the International Labor Office met today to discuss the above resolution. The Indian labor representative Yao Hee and the Chinese government representative Li Pingheng supported it, arguing that this standing committee should hold meetings in rotation in various Asian countries, and that representatives from all Asian countries should participate, and not be limited to representatives from China, Japan, and India alone. The Indian government representative, Sir Ramaswami Mudaliar, criticized Yao Hee's proposal and requested the establishment of a sub-committee to study the two issues of establishing a standing committee and convening an Asian labor conference. The Japanese government representative, Kitaoka, supported Sir Ramaswami Mudaliar's opinion, as did the Canadian government representative, Leggett, who said that all countries with interests in Asia should be allowed to participate in the standing committee. (Havas News Agency, 12th)

The Number of Armies in Various Countries Around the World Has Increased by 2 Million Compared to Before World War I, Not Including Semi-Military Groups

(Geneva) The League of Nations Secretariat issued statistics today stating that the current number of troops in various countries is 2 million more than at the beginning of World War I. There are currently 8.1 million soldiers in the world. Semi-military groups, such as the German Nazi stormtroopers and the Italian Blackshirts, are not included. (National News Agency, 12th)

Air Battle Between Two Armies Near Madrid, Spain, Government Denies Using Poison Gas, Continued Progress in the Counter-Offensive South of the Capital

Madrid Several government aircraft and rebel aircraft engaged in their first air war over the capital this morning, lasting 30 minutes. Six rebel aircraft were hit, burned, and crashed to the ground. Two government aircraft were also shot down. According to official war reports, the government army launched an offensive at dawn today and was quite successful. (National News Agency, 13th)

Madrid The reduction in artillery fire from both sides over the past twelve hours suggests that the Nationalists' advance has been hampered, or that the artillery positions of that army have been destroyed by government aircraft. An air battle occurred in Madrid today, and at least one Nationalist aircraft was shot down. At present, the Nationalists seem to have concentrated elite troops on the Toledo Avenue, and the next major offensive will begin from there. Although the city of Madrid has been bombarded by artillery fire, the residents remain calm. The government has fresh troops with a strong military presence coming from Catalonia, and solemnly denies that poison gas was used in the fighting with the Nationalist army. (Reuters, 13th)

Madrid The government gazette announced today that government troops have recaptured the Getafe airfield, and the threat of the rebels cutting off traffic to the capital has been greatly reduced. The government army's heavy artillery has also inflicted heavy damage on the rebels. The morale of the government army has been greatly boosted, and reports from other parties also indicate that the government army is winning on all fronts. (National News Agency, 12th)

Madrid According to semi-official sources, government troops have recaptured Getafe and other villages near the capital. A small detachment of Moors was completely surrounded by government troops in the Casa de Campo area in the western suburbs of the capital and was in a difficult situation. It is reported that in last night's fierce battle, the Nationalist army used its elite infantry, assisted by artillery and tanks. This small detachment of Moorish troops was far away from the main army, which led to their encirclement. The government army repelled the attackers, and then received reinforcements from two battalions of fresh troops, and launched a fierce counter-offensive, causing heavy damage to the Nationalist army, which was forced to retreat. It is reported that the corpses of foreign legionnaires and Moors are scattered everywhere. The government army claims to have captured 200 enemies and seized thousands of rifles. The surrounded Moorish soldiers are well-equipped with automatic weapons, but many believe that they will eventually surrender due to the heavy bombardment by the government army's artillery and the shooting from various high-rise buildings. The Nationalist army's artillery bombardment was even stronger today, and the rumbling sound shook the entire city. (Reuters, 12th)

Lisbon It is undeniable that poison gas has been widely used in the Spanish Civil War. It has been used for 118 days now. According to news from the front line, Nationalist army officers have told people that the government army has used poison gas bombs in an attempt to disperse the Nationalist army. Therefore, the Nationalist army may be forced to use poison gas as well. According to a recent telegram from Reuters' front-line reporter, there has been no change in the positions of the two armies in the past 24 hours. The reports that the government militia has recaptured Madrid's Getafe airfield and repelled the Nationalist army in Casa de Campo, the site of the former king's private garden, seem to be exaggerated. Reuters' Madrid reporter reported by long-distance telephone this morning that government aircraft did bomb the Getafe airfield yesterday. At the same time, Reuters' special reporter accompanying the Nationalist army west of the Manzanares River also telegraphed last night that the Moroccan army could only advance half a mile on the Casa de Campo to Toledo front line. It is reported that the government's ability to prevent the Nationalist army from advancing in the past five days has been entirely due to the newly produced 20mm anti-tank guns and the well-trained and accurate gunners. The Nationalist army often uses tanks as a tool for charging during its advance, but it has unexpectedly encountered strong opponents in recent days. The anti-tank guns used by the government militia fire extremely accurately, causing heavy damage and greatly reducing the chance of advancement. According to reports from all sides, there are many women among the government's fallen soldiers. (Reuters, 13th)

Rebels Optimistic About the War, Strategic Emphasis on Artillery Bombardment

Talavera de la Reina (100 kilometers southwest of Madrid) A special dispatch from our reporter: People in the Nationalist army here are optimistic about the future of the war. According to the authorities, a small detachment of Nationalist troops crossed the Manzanares River (outside the south gate of Madrid) last night for reconnaissance. At the same time, a column led by Colonel Yague, using tanks and artillery as cover, advanced towards Madrid, now only 100 meters away from the rooftops of the city. The weather was bad yesterday, and the aircraft of the Nationalist army were unable to fly out, but they plan to fly to Madrid tomorrow to drop leaflets, advising residents to flee to the safe zone in the northeast corner of the capital to avoid relentless bombs. The General Headquarters here is now focusing on artillery bombardment due to the government army's determination to resist and its willingness to die in battle. If infantry is used to attack the city, many lives will be sacrificed. For example, the "North Station" in the city, which was originally a trench dug by the government army for defense, is also the place where the Nationalist army's artillery fire is concentrated. Every day, shells fall like rain, and part of it has now been destroyed. In addition, there have been several large fires in Madrid in recent days. One of them occurred in a gas plant and has been burning for three days without being extinguished. Regarding the war situation, the battle at the "Toledo" bridge outside the south gate of Madrid and the town of Carabanchel, six kilometers away from the city, was very fierce yesterday. The government army had many machine guns lined up in the "Toledo" bridge area, and gun emplacements were also installed in the houses in the town of Carabanchel, but they were eventually captured by the Nationalist army. Afterwards, 300 corpses of government soldiers were found in the Carabanchel town hospital. In a trench, 30 members of the government militia were found, all breathless, but still tightly holding machine guns, which shows their courage in resistance. (Havas News Agency, 13th)

Madrid A special dispatch from our reporter: The weather was bad on the southern front of the capital yesterday, and the line of sight was unclear. Therefore, the aircraft of the Nationalist army were unable to sortie, and only the artillery bombarded the government army's positions. The government army also returned fire. In the evening, the artillery battle between the two armies was fierce. Before long, the government army's artillery fire stopped abruptly. At that time, looking from the Nationalist army's front line, smoke and fire were seen billowing near the highway from the western suburbs of Madrid to the province of Extremadura. Most of the houses there must have been hit and caught fire. (Havas News Agency, 13th)

Franco Does Not Advocate Impatience, Government Aircraft Strafe Enemy Troops

Lisbon Many military experts here say that the reason why the Spanish Nationalist army has been slow to attack the capital is a strategy of General Franco, the commander-in-chief. Franco plans to deplete the enemy's combat power in the suburbs of the capital. Then, when the Nationalist army enters the city, the enemy will be exhausted and unable to fight fiercely in the streets. Thus, the Nationalist army can lose fewer lives. Therefore, even when the government militia seems to be weak, Franco is still unwilling to sacrifice lives and launch an all-out attack. A Nationalist army tank, with a Portuguese man inside, advanced to a certain point in the city yesterday, but was eventually forced to withdraw. Although a large number of guards chased and bombarded it during the withdrawal, it was still able to escape danger. This proves that the Nationalist army has mechanized units to help. If they are willing to engage in street fighting, they could have made greater progress than they have today in the past few days. (Reuters, 13th)

Madrid The National Defense Committee recently issued a communique stating, "Fifteen government aircraft flew to the vicinity of the capital yesterday afternoon to conduct reconnaissance. There were no traces of enemy troops in the Casa de Campo park in the western suburbs, but large numbers of enemy troops were seen concentrated in the towns of Upper Carabanchel and Lower Carabanchel in the southern suburbs, including infantry, cavalry, and tank units. Each of these aircraft was equipped with machine guns, four per aircraft, for a total of sixty. They immediately flew low and strafed the enemy troops with machine guns. The rebels were caught off guard. Although they opened anti-aircraft fire, they failed to hit anything, and fled in all directions, abandoning countless corpses and wounded. Unfortunately, due to bad weather, two of the government aircraft touched the Guadarrama Mountains in the dense fog, causing them to crash." (Havas News Agency, 13th)

Diplomatic Corps Agrees to Assist in Protecting the Safety of Citizens in the Capital

Madrid – Foreign Minister Téllez Juaréz and Minister of Justice Olivan recently arrived here from the port of Valencia. They immediately convened the National Defense Committee (i.e., those responsible for remaining on duty) to discuss the war situation, in order to return to the port of Valencia and report to the Cabellero cabinet. It is generally understood that the meeting resulted in several important resolutions. Furthermore, the diplomatic corps proposed to the National Defense Committee to cooperate in protecting the safety of civilians within the city of Madrid, which was accepted by the committee. To this end, a Civilian Safety Protection Committee was established, with the Mexican Ambassador to Spain as Chairman, and representatives from the United Kingdom and Argentina as Vice-Chairmen. (Havas dispatch, 12th)

Russian Ships Transport Supplies

Valencia City – The Soviet Russian ship "Komsomol" arrived here recently, carrying 22,000 sets of children's clothing, 2,847 tons of corn, 1,000 tons of flour, 43 tons of sturgeon, 50 tons of Italian pasta and rapeseed sauce. It was immediately unloaded and brought ashore for the use of supporting the military and civilians. When the ship's crew went ashore, the residents cheered them warmly. In the evening, a famous play was performed at the Apolo Theatre to entertain them. (Havas dispatch, 13th)

French Left-Wing Parliamentarians Discuss the Situation in Spain, Planning to Request the Government to Restore Freedom of Trade with Spain

(Paris) Representatives from the left-wing parties, i.e., the majority parties, in the Chamber of Deputies are scheduled to meet today to discuss the non-intervention issue in the Spanish Civil War. They will also visit Prime Minister Blum to request the restoration of free trade with the Spanish Republic. (Havas dispatch, 13th)

Neutrality Committee Meeting, Intense Arguments between Italian and Russian Representatives, Unanimously Adopted Supervisory Measures

(London) The Adjustment Committee of the Non-Intervention Agreement on the Spanish Civil War held a long meeting yesterday afternoon. The Italian and Russian representatives engaged in mutual accusations during the meeting, which extended to 9:30 PM, lasting a total of five and a half hours. A communiqué released after midnight declared that the committee had approved the plan to establish a supervisory system in Spain, but it could only be implemented after the governments concerned had submitted amended drafts and approved them. The Italian and Russian representatives engaged in heated debate, with the Italian representative accusing the Soviet Union of interfering in Spanish affairs, stating that the Soviet Union's creed was a creed of war, and that not only the future of Spain, but the future of all civilized countries in Europe was in danger. The Soviet Russian representative responded that the Italian representative was playing a German-made tune, and that the distinction today was not between communism and fascism, but between war and peace, that is, between countries that glorified aggressive war and countries that abhorred war and desired peace. Italy had removed its mask and stood openly before the world as an aggressor and a destroyer of treaties. The committee considered four complaints filed by the Soviet Union regarding Italy's violation of the Non-Intervention Agreement, but due to insufficient evidence, the committee was unable to determine that Italy had violated the agreement. (Reuters dispatch, 13th)

(London) The Adjustment Committee of the Non-Intervention in the Spanish Civil War held a plenary session at 4 PM today, at which the outline of the Supervisory Committee's plan was unanimously adopted. This committee will consist of two, working separately in the territories controlled by the Spanish government forces and the Nationalist forces, to monitor the Spanish-Portuguese border, as well as Spanish ports and airfields. It is estimated that the Supervisory Committee will require 1,000 personnel, at a cost of no less than one million pounds. Regarding this matter, the Adjustment Committee submitted a reservation, to be consulted with their respective governments to determine whether the number of personnel could be appropriately reduced. In addition, the Soviet government had previously submitted a reply to the accusations by other countries of violating the Non-Intervention Agreement. The Adjustment Committee specifically reviewed it today. After discussion, except for one point that still required further investigation, the rest were considered satisfactory. During the discussion, there was a heated argument between the Italian and Russian representatives. (Havas dispatch, 12th)

Complete Agreement on Three Major Issues

(Vienna) According to informed sources, in addition to what has already been stated in the communiqué, the Italian-Austrian-Hungarian Protocol signed today also mentions the following issues: (1) Amendment of the League of Nations Covenant; (2) The struggle against communism; (3) The three countries may grant recognition to the Spanish Nationalist government in the future, but the date of recognition has not yet been decided; (4) Regarding the Locarno Five-Power Conference, the three countries have decided to adopt Italy's opinion. In addition, the issue of the restoration of the Austrian Habsburg royal family was not mentioned in the protocol. Regarding the first issue above, it is heard that the three governments agreed to use the speech made by Austrian Foreign Minister Schmidt at the League of Nations General Assembly in September as the basis for amending the covenant. Schmidt's speech advocated three points: (1) The League of Nations should be universalized; (2) Various issues should not be resolved through secret diplomacy; (3) The League of Nations Covenant should be separated from the various peace treaties of the European War. Regarding the second issue, the struggle against communism, the Italian, Austrian, and Hungarian governments did not endorse the German government's suggestion to organize an anti-communist crusade, but advocated that the three countries should adopt a policy of joint cooperation to oppose communist propaganda within their respective countries. Furthermore, after the signing of this month's three-nation protocol, Italian Foreign Minister Count Ciano gave a speech to the press, stating that the Italian and Austrian governments had decided to continue to adopt a constructive policy, similar to the Rome Protocols jointly signed by Italian Prime Minister Mussolini, the late Hungarian Prime Minister Gömbös, and the late Austrian Chancellor Dollfuss in March 1934. This was the beginning of this constructive policy, and it should naturally continue to be followed. The Hungarian Foreign Minister, Kanya, also gave a speech to the press, saying that he firmly believed that the achievements of the three-nation conference would strengthen the peace situation. (Havas dispatch, 12th)

Hungary Feels Disappointed That Border Revisions Were Not Mentioned

Budapest – The Italian, Austrian, and Hungarian foreign ministers did not mention Hungary's request for border revisions in the protocol signed in Vienna today. This is quite disappointing to Hungarian political circles, as they are satisfied with Italy and Austria's open support for Hungary's request to rearm, but in addition to this, they still hoped to obtain more practical results. Now that this is not the case, they cannot help but feel disappointed. In addition, political figures believe that the Austrian and Hungarian recognition of Italy's annexation of Abyssinia was expected. The fact that the communiqué issued after the signing of the three-nation protocol used rather vague language regarding Germany is due to Italy's concern about Austria's independence. As for the statement in the communiqué that "the three countries will respectively conclude bilateral agreements to develop trade relations," political figures did not comment on it, only stating that the trade relations between Italy and Hungary have been greatly affected since the devaluation of the Italian lira, and have not yet improved. Official sources, on the other hand, said that the results of the Vienna three-nation conference are quite satisfactory, as the friendship between Italy, Austria, and Hungary will be further strengthened as a result. (Havas dispatch, 12th)

The Little Entente Expresses Resentment at the Three Countries' Unilateral Action

Bucharest – After the Italian, Austrian, and Hungarian foreign ministers' meeting recognized Hungary's right to military equality, political figures here are very resentful, believing that although Austria has restored conscription, Hungary should not follow suit, because Austria can say that its borders are threatened, while Hungary has no such excuse. (Havas dispatch, 13th)

Prague – Political figures recently declared that the Italian, Austrian, and Hungarian foreign ministers' meeting's recognition of Hungary's right to military equality is a unilateral action by those countries, which is related to the entire Little Entente, not just Czechoslovakia. It must be understood that all issues can be resolved through negotiations, but unilateral actions are strongly opposed by the countries of the Little Entente. (Havas dispatch, 13th)

Belgrade – Italian Prime Minister Mussolini expressed support for Hungary's claim to revise the treaty earlier, and the Italian, Austrian, and Hungarian foreign ministers' meeting later recognized Hungary's right to military equality. Officials here recently explained that this is merely an empty expression to Hungary, with only a superficial appearance. Otherwise, the countries of the Little Entente will take effective self-defense measures in response as soon as the military clauses contained in the Treaty of Trianon are violated. As for the actual results achieved by the Italian, Austrian, and Hungarian foreign ministers' meeting, since the signatory countries of the Rome Protocol can use gradual and fundamental methods to improve mutual relations with other countries in the Danube region, Yugoslavia, while remaining committed to the regional security system established by the Little Entente, will not refuse the establishment of bilateral agreements between the signatory countries of the Rome Protocol. In short, Yugoslavia is eagerly anticipating closer relations with Italy. (Havas dispatch, 12th)

Italian Foreign Minister Arrives in Budapest, Receives a Warm Welcome

Budapest – Italian Foreign Minister Count Ciano arrived here at 1:10 PM today. Hungarian Prime Minister Darányi, personnel from the Italian Embassy, representatives from the Italian Fascist Party branch, and most Italian expatriates welcomed him at the station. After Count Ciano alighted from the train, he inspected a company of infantry and a company of Hungarian youth corps at the station. Then, amid the cheers of the crowd, he traveled by car to his residence to rest. Italian and Hungarian national flags were displayed along the route, creating a lively atmosphere. When the car arrived at the residence, the crowd gathered outside the gate, cheering and paying their respects. Count Ciano then stepped out onto the balcony to express his gratitude. (Havas dispatch, 13th)

League of Nations Seeks Opinions on Amending the Covenant, Forty Countries Have Responded

(Geneva) The Secretariat of the League of Nations previously sought opinions from member states regarding the amendment of the Covenant, in accordance with the resolution passed by the special session of the League of Nations General Assembly in July. As of now, forty countries have submitted replies. Belgium's reply has also arrived, and its full text will be published tomorrow. (Havas dispatch, 12th)

This Year's Nobel Prize Winners: Literature, Chemistry, Physics

Stockholm – The 1936 Nobel Prize in Literature has been awarded to the famous American playwright Eugene O'Neill. The Physics Prize will be shared by Professor Hess of the University of Innsbruck in Austria and Dr. Anderson of the California Institute of Technology in the United States. The Chemistry Prize will be awarded to Professor Debye of Berlin for his contribution to molecular structure. The Nobel Prize is a donation from Alfred Nobel, the famous Swedish scientist who invented dynamite. The prize money is distributed by the Board of Trustees from the income of the fund. Nobel died on December 10, 1896, leaving an estate of 1.75 million pounds. The first prize was awarded on the fifth anniversary of Nobel's death, and it has since been stipulated that a decision will be made annually, divided into several categories: physics, chemistry, physiology or medicine, literature, and those who have made the most significant contributions to peace. In 1935, each prize exceeded 10,000 pounds. Eugene O'Neill, who won the Literature Prize this year, is not only the greatest playwright in the United States, but has also gained international fame. (Reuters dispatch, 13th)

Vienna Conference Acknowledges Equal Military Rights for Hungary and Austria, Three Countries Established Coordination on General Issues, Bilateral Agreements to Develop Trade to be Reached

Vienna – The Three-Nation Conference of Italy, Austria, and Hungary concluded today, and a communiqué was issued acknowledging Hungary's equal military rights. This move indicates that Hungary has followed in the footsteps of Germany and Austria in abolishing the military constraints of the peace treaty, and can now implement conscription and carry out large-scale military restoration. (National Telegram, 12th)

Vienna – The Italian, Austrian, and Hungarian foreign ministers signed the Three-Nation Protocol at 5:30 PM today. After the signing, a communiqué was immediately issued, stating that the Three-Nation Conference recognized the legitimacy of the demands by Austria and Hungary for equal military rights. This demand is based on "the fundamental principles of justice." The governments of Italy, Austria, and Hungary will now maintain constant contact with each other to enhance these principles. Italy will also consider Austria and Hungary's expectations of participating in the economic development of Abyssinia. In addition, the communiqué also stated that Italy, Austria, and Hungary have reached a satisfactory agreement on general issues directly related to the three countries. As for the economic cooperation between the three countries, there will be no changes at this time. Italy, Austria, and Hungary will respectively conclude bilateral agreements to develop mutual trade relations. Regarding the relations between Germany and Austria after the signing of the German-Austrian Agreement on July 11, Austrian Foreign Minister Schmidt presented a report, which was considered satisfactory by Italian Foreign Minister Count Ciano and Hungarian Foreign Minister Kanya. The Austrian and Hungarian foreign ministers were also satisfied that Germany and Italy had decided to cooperate amicably in the Danube region after Count Ciano visited Germany and held talks with Chancellor Hitler and Foreign Minister von Neurath. The three governments reiterated that the supplementary clauses to the Rome Protocols signed by Italy, Austria, and Hungary in March of this year are still in effect. Austria and Hungary also legally recognized Italy's annexation of Abyssinia. The various issues discussed above and the results achieved have now been recorded in a protocol signed by Italy, Austria, and Hungary. The communiqué concludes by announcing that the next Three-Nation Conference will be held in the Hungarian capital, but the date has not yet been determined. (Havas dispatch, 12th)

Seventeenth Session of the League of Nations Assembly (Continued 2)

1. The Abyssinian Representative Qualification Issue... 2. The Work of Our Country's Representatives in Various Committees (A) First Committee (B) Second Committee (C) Third Committee (D) Fourth Committee (E) Fifth Committee on Mining (F) Sixth Committee... 3. The Reorganization Issue of the League of Nations... 4. The Speech of Our Representative in the General Discussion of the Assembly... 5. The Process of Our Country's Election as Member of the Administrative Council and Judge of the Hague... 6. Conclusion...

B. Second Committee

This committee specializes in discussing financial, economic, and health issues. Regarding health, the committee passed a proposal to prepare for the Far East Rural Hygiene Conference in Java next year. Our representative, Mr. Jin, stood up and expressed his opinion, stating that our country is one of the most important countries in international cooperation, and therefore feels particularly interested in the aforementioned Far East Rural Hygiene Conference. Our delegation sincerely hopes for the success of the conference, he said. The committee then discussed the financial and economic situations of various countries. At the time, France, the Netherlands, and Switzerland had just begun to devalue their currencies, which provided many representatives with the opportunity to speak. Our representative, Mr. Jin, stood up to explain the economic situation of our country in recent years, stating that our country has received assistance from friendly banks, especially the assistance of the British government, and therefore has achieved great success since the implementation of the legal currency. Finally, it has also received the approval of the United States, so our country's formal foreign trade has embarked on the right track, which is very obvious. At the same time, it can further prove that our country's currency reform is actually beneficial to foreign traders in our country. Mr. Jin continued to say that the devaluation of a national bank's currency is enough to revitalize international trade. Our country feels delighted and is happy to follow the new trend of international trade, and is grateful that the world economy will recover and prosper again. Our country will again become the world's market. Finally, Mr. Jin raised international attention to the seriousness of smuggling in North China and its impact on our country's national economy, people's livelihood, and international trade, and hoped for international cooperation to resolve this difficulty.

C. Third Committee Regarding

The organization and purpose of the committee have already been described earlier. As for the Disarmament Conference, small countries, needless to say, strongly hope that the conference will be revived in order to work towards future peace. Even the opinions of major countries such as England, France, and Russia are very consistent, and they also advocate the organization of a permanent committee to specialize in studying disarmament issues and the procedures for convening the conference. After a heated debate, the committee passed its report and transferred it to the General Assembly. The report consists of fifteen sections, stating the committee's opinions on the Disarmament Conference, and passing the following proposal: "The General Assembly firmly believes in the need to continue and intensify efforts to reduce armaments in order to implement Article 8 of the League of Nations, and warmly welcomes the organization of a Disarmament Conference at an early date. The committee hereby requests the Administrative Council to inform the governments of all countries that previously participated in the Disarmament Conference of the Third Committee's report on this issue and its meeting minutes." This proposal and report have been passed by the General Assembly, and the long-dormant World Disarmament Conference has a glimmer of hope. Although there are still many difficulties, it can be said to be one of the achievements of this session of the League of Nations Assembly. If all countries can show their sincerity in disarmament in the future, and the people of the world do not forget to continue their efforts for peace, future peace may not be impossible to expect.

D. Fourth Committee

This committee specializes in discussing the work and expenses of the Secretariat, the League of Nations budget, and the membership fees of various member states. Our representative, Mr. Liang, expressed his opinion, stating that the management work of the Secretariat is extremely important, so various tasks must be implemented in a rational manner, because whether the League of Nations can win the trust of the people of various countries is closely related to it. Regarding the issue of the Secretariat's staff, our representative, Mr. Liang, said that our country pays more than 1.2 million gold francs in membership fees every year, but there is only one Chinese staff member in the Secretariat. This is certainly not the Secretary-General's mistake, but it is hoped that when our country recommends staff, the Secretariat must accept them. Mr. Liang continued to say that some countries have many members in various agencies of the Secretariat, so the salaries they pay almost exceed the total amount of membership fees their country pays each year, while some countries do not even have a single staff member in the Secretariat. The annual salary obtained by Chinese staff from the Secretariat is only equal to three percent of the annual fee paid by our country. Therefore, our delegation reserves the right to recommend staff for future concrete proposals, he said. The reporter feels that Mr. Liang's proposal is quite important and is an event that our delegation should have paid attention to in the past. If we want to rectify diplomacy in Geneva, the staff in the Secretariat can provide various convenient assistance. It goes without saying that the various main tasks of the Secretariat have always been controlled by a small number of staff. Even many small countries, compared to the membership fees they pay each year, are less than one-fifth of our country, but their positions as staff in the Secretariat are often more superior than those of Chinese staff. Therefore, when the League of Nations has problems related to their country, various procedures and important information have already been prepared before their country's representatives arrive in Geneva. The salary issue is certainly decided. Our country certainly does not hope to be fully compensated for its losses, but at the very least, it cannot only fulfill its obligations without enjoying its rights. Especially in order to make our country's relationship with the League of Nations closer and to achieve practical cooperation, at least one Chinese staff member is needed in each of the information, legal, political, cultural, cooperation, opium, transportation, transportation, financial, and economic departments. This is due to the fact that since Secretary-General Avenol took office, he has failed to rationalize the distribution of the Secretariat's staff and has pursued policies that are often unbalanced. We hope that he can have considerable awareness and correct this. On the other hand, it is reported that our delegation has made considerable preparations for the above issue and is preparing to submit a list. It is also reported that there are four candidates on each list, and the League of Nations Secretariat is preparing to accept two of them. Regardless of whether it is true or not, or regardless of who is recommended, we feel that there are several important conditions that our delegation must pay attention to. First, the person recommended must not be coming for a job, and should not have the mentality of securing a position. At the very least, the person should be able to take responsibility and make considerable contributions to both the League of Nations and our side. Second, there is no need to ask about the person's private relationships or their status in their own country, but attention must be paid to their character and morality. It is better not to recommend someone than to recommend someone with bad behavior, which would damage the credibility of recommending staff. Third, the person must meet the requirements in terms of excellent academic knowledge and language skills, and efforts must be made to match the person's strengths with the work they are recommended for, so that they can achieve considerable results. Moreover, such people can be trained as experts in a relatively short period of time and can make considerable contributions to the work of the League of Nations and to the future of our country. If our delegation can carefully select staff based on the above or more complete conditions, the work in Geneva will certainly not feel constrained in the future.

E. Fifth Committee In this committee, the issue related to our country is the opium issue. When the committee discussed the report of the Opium Advisory Committee, the Portuguese representative spoke, stating that it is necessary to discuss the restriction of the production of raw materials for narcotics. According to the number of legitimate needs in the world, it is 540,000 tons. However, in fact, the production of raw and prepared opium and narcotics in the world exceeded the above number by 1,000 tons in 1933 and 540 tons in 1934. This figure does not include the 12,000 tons of Chinese opium and narcotics produced annually. The importance of restricting the production of the above raw materials is very obvious, he said. He continued to say that under this kind of production restriction, countless Chinese farmers continue to plant 100,000 hectares of opium poppies every year. We have nothing to say to China, he said. Our representative, Mr. Qian, replied, stating that the main difficulty for our government in banning drugs is that it cannot be effective without international cooperation. If the Opium Advisory Committee informs the countries concerned to take all possible measures to crack down on their people engaging in illegal sales in our country and severely punish this kind of trade, our government will do its best to make further efforts in the implementation of our national drug ban plan. Regarding the number of narcotics produced in our country mentioned by the Portuguese representative, our representative, Mr. Qian, replied, stating that the number of narcotics produced in China mentioned by the Portuguese representative was extracted from the report of the Opium Advisory Committee. Our representative has already proposed revisions to this number, but the Portuguese representative insisted that this number is in the report and that the number is very accurate, he said. When our representative, Mr. Qian, pointed out that our representative in the report's meeting minutes had reservations about the 12,000-ton figure mentioned by the American representative as proof, the Portuguese representative remained silent and did not answer. The report was then passed.

(To be continued)

Bandit-Puppet-Mongolian Troops Invade Sui. Wuchuan Situation Suddenly Tense. Planning to Invade Sui Border in Three Routes. Over a Hundred Military Officers from a Certain Side Go to Supervise the Battle.

Zhangbei Correspondence: The serious situation on the border of Sui province, after shifting from Suidong to Suibei, has seen bandit, puppet, and Mongolian troops gather in Suibei in recent days. Under the cover of airplanes and tanks from a certain side, they are attacking Suibei from Bailingmiao every day, with the aim of capturing Wuchuan and approaching Guisui. Therefore, the situation in Wuchuan is suddenly becoming serious. However, every determined attack only involves a small number of troops and has been repelled by the defending forces and militia. They have not succeeded. Although the atmosphere is extremely tense, these are only small contacts and not yet a formal main force battle.

Puppet-Bandit Troops Gradually Dispatched. Planning to Invade Sui Border in Three Routes. Over a Hundred Military Officers from a Certain Side Go to Supervise the Battle.

Currently, bandit, puppet, and Mongolian troops are still being gradually dispatched. In addition to the cavalry participating in the invasion of Sui, Wang Ying's bandit troops are also marching towards Bailingmiao for concentration. Wang's bandit force currently only has over 5,000 men. The puppet Mongolian troops now scattered in various counties in Chahar North are only over 1,000 men. Most of them have already arrived in Bailingmiao. The 3,000 plus puppet Mongolian troops under Zhuo Shihai's command stationed in Niuyangqun are also moving towards Suibei and concentrating in Bailingmiao. The bandit troops who opened from Guyuan Chongli in the west a few days ago have now arrived in Shangdu. It is said that they will be slightly reorganized and also concentrated in Bailingmiao. The bandit troops from Rehe are still continuing to open to the west and are stationed in the Guyuan Chongli area. Two squadrons of a certain side's military force have now opened to Kangbao and Baochang and are advancing westward one after another. It is said that their major destination is also Bailingmiao. Recently, a certain side must send airplanes from Duolun and Shangdu every day to偵察 the situation of the Sui border positions. The ammunition of the bandit-puppet troops is still being transported westward by car from Duolun Zhangbei every day. The general supply station of the Chahar North armies has now been relocated to Duolun. This place is the supply station of Li Shouxin's puppet troops and only supplies Li's troops stationed in Daqinggou and Nanhaogan with ammunition and other materials.

Bandit Troops Attack Sui in Three Routes

The puppet-bandit-Mongolian troops are invading Suiyuan from Suibei, Suidong, and Suixi in three routes. The deployment of each route's front line is as follows: Bao Yueqing, Zhuo Shihai, and other Mongolian troops combine into one route and approach Wuchuan and Guisui from Suibei. Li Shouxin's troops, in addition to those in Qinggou and Nanhaogan, combine with Zhang Haipeng, Gan Jingxiu's entire force, the bandit troops from Rehe, and a certain side's squadron into one route and jointly attack Suidong. Wang Ying's troops will wait for the bandit-Mongolian troops to concentrate in Bailingmiao before combining into one route and taking Guyang along the north side of Yinshan. After succeeding, Wang will immediately lead his infantry and cavalry directly to Baotou and penetrate deep into Suixi and the Hetao. Currently, most of Li Shouxin's artillery is in Nanhaogan. Those concentrated in Shangdu are mostly cavalry. Li himself remains in Shangdu to command everything. Over a hundred military officers from a certain side arrived at Jiabusi on the eighth of this month and will soon go to Shangdu and Bailingmiao to infiltrate Li Shouxin's and Wang Ying's puppet-bandit troops to command and supervise the battle.

Grain Prices Soar in Various Counties in Chahar North

In the past, grain carts from various counties in Chahar North often went to Xinghe and Jining (Pingdiquan) in Suidong to purchase grain. Now, due to the tense situation, they can no longer go. Coal from Suiyuan and Jinbei has also stopped being transported recently, causing extreme panic in various counties in Chahar North regarding food and fuel. Grain prices have therefore soared endlessly. Furthermore, the frequent redeployment of puppet-bandit troops, such as replenishing military supplies and paying for transit and departure expenses, has overwhelmed merchants. The burden on the people in various counties has increased sixfold compared to the past, causing everyone to frown and wail.

Songjiang Bureau Chief Periodically Replaced

Songjiang County Public Security Bureau Chief He Runzhang has been ordered to be transferred to Nantong Public Security Bureau in exchange for Bureau Chief Song Mingqi. It is reported that Bureau Chief Song is scheduled to come to Songjiang on the 16th to take over, and Bureau Chief He is scheduled to leave Songjiang on the 17th to take up his new post in Nantong. Chief He has been in Songjiang for two years and has achieved remarkable political achievements. In addition to the presentation of souvenirs by various circles, the beggars housed in the beggar shelter used their daily alms to make a silver shield with the words "Kindness Like Parents" engraved on it. Chief He also gave away four dozen towels as souvenirs.

Jiading Daytime Robbery Injures People

At noon on the 12th, Xiao Changsheng, a robber from Hunan, wearing short clothes and sneakers, carried two box guns and went to the Wuchang Candle Shop on Nanxiang East Street, pretending to borrow money from the shop assistant. Taking advantage of the unpreparedness of the people, he robbed twelve yuan in legal currency from the counter and fled. Two shop assistants secretly followed him. First they went east, then turned southwest, approaching the Nan Street Public Security Branch Bureau. The two shop assistants shouted loudly to catch the robber. The robber opened fire, first to the south and then to the north. One bullet hit Hou Jinyuan, the owner of the Hou Zhenyuan leather suitcase shop, in the left shoulder. One bullet hit Yang A Jin, the temple priest of Xianjing Hall, in the right kneecap. Qian, the acting chief of the Public Security Branch Bureau, immediately led the police to pursue the robber after hearing the news. The robber escaped to the intersection of the Shanghai-Suzhou and Shanghai-Wuxi roads and the bamboo forest west of the stadium, and opened fire on the pursuing police one after another. The police returned fire on one side and chased on the other side. At the train station, the robber opened fire and wounded a passerby. The Xiang Station Security Team police came out to assist in the arrest. The robber fled west. The team police chased for more than twenty miles and finally captured him in Lujiaxing Town in Qingpu County. After being briefly interrogated by the Security Team headquarters, he was escorted to the county to be dealt with according to law at noon on the 13th.

Suzhou Bandit Alarm Amidst Winter Defense

Bandit ships were discovered in the Luoxiang area of Weiting, Suxiang, a few days ago, carrying more than 20 bandits, plotting wrongdoing. The matter was learned by the villagers, who fired shots as a warning. The bandits escaped to the Yangcheng River. The police pursued them but did not capture them. Unexpectedly, six bandit ships were also discovered in the Luowei area of Xujiagang, Zhouzhuang Township, at 5 pm on the 12th. It is not known whether they were the bandits discovered in Weiting Township. The township water patrol team happened to be patrolling the area and encountered the bandits and opened fire. They held out for about an hour. As a result, one bandit was killed, more than ten bandits were captured, and four bandit ships were seized. The remaining bandits escaped by swimming. The captured bandits have been escorted to the team headquarters for interrogation on the 13th. In addition, the Jiangzhe Bandit Suppression Joint Office sent investigators to Suzhou to work with the Public Security Bureau to capture a habitual bandit named Wang Zibin outside the Banmen in Sanli灣. He has been escorted to the office for interrogation. It is reported that the bandit committed many crimes and was wanted by the Taihu Bandit Suppression Headquarters. Also, late at night on the 12th, Lü Jinpei, a fellow worker at the Jiutai pig business in the Lianhuadou area of the Banmen外猪行河头, was carrying money to Zhenjiang to buy pigs. While passing through the area, he suddenly encountered six bandits who tied Lü up and robbed him of more than fifty yuan in legal currency. After passersby untied Lü, he immediately reported it to the police district in charge, who immediately sent police to pursue the bandits but did not catch them. Only a bag of clothes was found, which was also an item that Lü Jinpei had been robbed of. The Public Security Bureau was immediately notified to request a search. Zhang Hanwei, the Chief of the Public Security Bureau, considered that it was the time of winter defense and the situation was unstable, and the bandits dared to rob in the urban area. On the 13th, he ordered his subordinates to solve the case within a limited time and bring the perpetrators to justice in order to maintain local security.

Rehearsal of Electric Echo

The Military Commission's Circulating Defense Observation Exhibition was held in Suzhou for five days to instill air defense knowledge to the public, with over 300,000 viewers, achieving very good results. The electric echo, organized by the local military and political authorities, has been rehearsed three times. A large-scale rehearsal was held on the 13th to examine the public's attention. In consultation with the New Transportation Promotion Association, it started simultaneously on land and water at 10 am on the 13th, temporarily stopping traffic for two hours. All Suzhou Boy Scouts and female ambulance personnel participated in the work, and the order was very good. The rehearsal will continue that night.

Wuxi Female Worker Dies from Abortion

Li Erjie, a 42-year-old female worker from No. 62 Huaxinli Workshop outside the East Gate of this county, is from Hujiadu, District 5. Her husband, Sun Er, from Xizhang, works as a boatman. Initially, the couple had a harmonious relationship and had one son and two daughters. Later, Erjie entered the Ruichangyong Silk Factory as a female worker and had some savings in hand. She had an affair with Xu Yongqing, the foreman of the factory, and regarded her husband as a thorn in her side. She claimed to eat vegetarian food and was determined to separate from her husband. Unexpectedly, after a few nights with Xu Yongqing, she became pregnant. She then tried to have an abortion. Starting on the 31st of last month, Xu Yongqing bought a package of silver nitrate every day and gave it to Erjie to swallow. Unexpectedly, the toxicity flared up and her stomach pain was excruciating. The fetus did not come down, and she died at 9 am yesterday (the 13th). Her husband, Sun Er, heard the news and immediately came to the city to negotiate with Xu Yongqing. At the same time, the Xijing Town Township Office reported to the Tingziqiao Public Security Police Station and summoned the deceased's family member Sun Er, the deceased's daughter Sun Xiangdi, and the neighbor Yu Ajin and the deceased's younger brother Li Binfu for interrogation. At the same time, Xie Xiaodi, the leader of Tianyi Tu, reported to the local court and requested an autopsy to verify and handle the matter.

Nantong Chongqi Land Property Rights Dispute

After the separation of Chongming and Qidong counties, most of the land property in Qidong belongs to Chongming landlords. The amount of rent collected each year reaches 1.6 million yuan. In recent years, Qidong has advocated that the land ownership of Chongming landlords be transferred to Qidong tenants. Chongming is extremely opposed. Ge, the special commissioner of the Fourth District, has been ordered by the provincial government to summon representatives from the two counties to 通 to discuss a solution.

Verdict in the Forged Telegram Case

Ding Zhusan, a telegram delivery man from the Nantong Telegraph Bureau, forged telegrams and sent them to various households in the countryside who often exchanged telegrams, defrauding them of special delivery fees. Wang Wuqiao, of Jinsha Yushun Porcelain Store, sent a forged telegram from Jingdezhen claiming that his father was sick, but when Wang rushed back, there was no such thing. Others, such as Sanyu Dayou Jin Company, Juegang Dayu Company, and Jinsha Xiechang Egg Shop, received forged telegrams fabricating market conditions and invited managers to Shanghai, all of which were deceived. They inquired with the Telegraph Bureau. Ding Zhusan was ordered by the Electric Administration Department of the Ministry of Communications to be transferred by the 통 Bureau to the court. On the 12th, Judge Bai of the Criminal Court completed the trial and sentenced the principal offender to one year and six months of imprisonment for the crime of repeatedly using forged private documents.

Haizhou Farmers Riot Against Work

Due to the accumulation of water in the flood land of Pangou Township in this county, the county government has requisitioned workers to dredge it and dispatched Du Kuangbin, the chief of the Public Security Section, to lead the security team members to supervise the work. Zhou, a farmer from Gaoxu Township, disobeyed orders regarding the work and suddenly summoned more than a hundred workers yesterday morning to carry out resistance work, injuring Wang, a member of the security team, and robbing him of a short gun and several bullets. Considering the seriousness of the situation, Chief Du flew to the county government to ask for instructions. After receiving the report, the county government dispatched dozens of security team members to the construction site this afternoon to suppress the situation. The injured security team member Wang has been sent to the Longhai Hospital for treatment.

Yangzhou Bandits Rob Zhuangding Boat in District Six

Zhuangding, who were being trained at the central people's school in District Six of Jiangdu, were scheduled to graduate in Yangzhou on the 12th of this month, as stipulated by the people's schools in each district. They gathered at the Zhunti Temple playground in the city for inspection. On the 10th, they formed a team at Guanling and came to Yangzhou by land. In addition, there were eight other people and two members of the town's merchant corps, Du Jintang and others, who unarmed escorted the entire team's luggage and supplies and came to Yangzhou by boat. At about 12 o'clock at night, while passing through Chenjiagou in Dongxiang, they suddenly heard a question from the shore about whether the boat was carrying Zhuangding from District Six. Those on the boat, suspecting that it was someone related to the school or the Zhuangding, answered in the affirmative. The shore immediately ordered the boat to stop, and they realized that they had encountered bandits. They did not dare to resist. Soon, seven or eight bandits, holding two Mauser pistols, two rifles, and three broadswords, boarded the boat and looted it. They knocked down Du Jintang, a member of the merchant corps who resisted, and fled ashore with the stolen goods.

Jiaxing Fire in Zhongjie

At more than 2 am on the 12th, a fire broke out in the warehouse of the Yuansheng Cigarette Shop in Zhongjie outside the North City of Jiaxing due to carelessness in frying peanuts. The flames immediately shot up into the sky and were unapproachable. The fire was extinguished only after the Yilong Fire Brigade of the entire city arrived at the scene to put out the fire. A total of Fuchangxing Grocery Store, Yuansheng Cigarette Shop, Tianxiangzhai Candy Store, and Shenhengxing Iron Store were burned down, with a total loss of five to six thousand yuan.

Hangzhou Major Fire at Lingyin Temple Yesterday

The Arhat Hall of Lingyin Temple in West Lake, which houses 500 golden Arhat statues sculpted by Anhui people with the surname Ren in the early Qing Dynasty, has been around for more than 300 years. Unexpectedly, at 3:15 pm on the 13th, a fire broke out due to the remaining fire from incense burned by pilgrims falling on the offering table. The fire was immediately unapproachable. The fire was extinguished after more than an hour after the fire brigade and fire association dispatched fire engines to put out the fire. It is estimated that the entire Arhat Hall and 500 golden Arhat statues were burned down, with a total loss of more than 100,000 yuan.

Preparing to Establish a Buddhist Temple and Monk Association

More than 40 abbots and nuns from important mountains in Hangzhou decided to establish a Buddhist Temple Association based on the provisions of the Regulations on Supervising Temples. A meeting was held at Jingci Temple on the 10th, and Rong Xu, Qin Liang, and others were elected as conveners and drafters. Seventeen preparatory members were appointed and a preparatory office was established, affiliated to Zhaqing Temple to start work. It was decided to echo the Buddhist Federation of Jiangsu and other provinces and deny that the Chinese Buddhist Association supported by a few philanthropists in Shanghai is a body representing the temples and monks of the country.

Yuyao Purchase Old Houses and Build Warehouses to Store Grain

The county government previously received an order from the province to build two warehouses with a capacity of 1.1 million catties of grain. It was stipulated that the construction cost of each warehouse should be at least 10,000 yuan. As it was difficult to raise funds for a while, the Construction Department approved a flexible approach. In addition to moving the Farmers Bank warehouse to serve as the county warehouse, the other warehouse was planned to be purchased and rebuilt at the former site of the Hushan Hefeng Flower Shop. The shareholders of the shop have agreed and a transfer contract was scheduled to be signed on the 10th. It is reported that the total selling price is 5,600 yuan. The county government also scheduled a joint meeting of the design and finance committees at 2 pm on the 13th to discuss warehouse matters.

Grand Banquet

Over 300 prominent figures from Chinese and American society have also been invited. The invitation reads, "Dear Sir/Madam, Our association, in order to expand Sino-American trade and enhance Sino-American friendship, has set a joint banquet at the American Club on Fuzhou Road, Shanghai, at 7:15 PM on the 20th of this month (Friday). We sincerely invite you to attend and share in the grand event. A reply card is attached for your convenience. Please fill it out and mail it back. We eagerly anticipate your presence. Sincerely, Sino-American Trade Association and American Chamber of Commerce, November 12th. Please wear a black mandarin jacket or black bow tie."

In addition to formally inviting people from all walks of life, all members of the Sino-American Trade Association jointly signed and sent invitation letters. Sincerely, Chen Guangfu, Guo Bingwen, Wang Xiaolai, Lin Kanghou, Bei Songsun, Zou Bingwen, Jin Runyang."

Demonstration of Telephone Communication

At the grand banquet on this day, China Aviation Company and China Electric Company will demonstrate aviation wireless telephone. At 9:00 PM that evening, two Chinese and two American guests will be invited to leave their seats and go to Longhua Airport to board a plane and fly around the city. While flying, they will converse with the guests at the banquet. This aviation telephone is a first in our country. In addition, we plan to hold the first Sino-American telephone call. This matter is currently being negotiated.

Mr. Wosaki Visited Mayor Wu Yesterday Regarding the Takase Case - Requested Assistance in Arresting the Culprit

Japanese Consul-General to Shanghai, Wosaki Yo, drove to the Municipal Government yesterday morning at 11:00 AM to visit Mayor Wu and requested assistance in arresting the culprit in the case of Japanese sailor Takase, which occurred in the concession on the evening of the 11th, and to protect Japanese residents. At that time, there was a period of alert, and after about an hour, all posts were removed. Gu Xinyi and Others Talk About - No Food Shortage This Year

New rice has been appearing on the market one after another, and the amount of goods arriving is surging daily. A reporter from New Voice News met with grain industry leaders Gu Xinyi and Jiang Shiya yesterday and learned that the city's existing rice supply consists of 300,000 dan of old rice, while there is no exact statistics on the new rice supply. This year, the rice production in various places, such as Henan, Anhui, Jiangxi, and Jiangsu provinces, has increased by 20%, an increase of 20 million dan compared with last year. Therefore, there is no need to order foreign rice this year, and the future of people's food supply can be said to be worry-free.
