Three Students Going to France to Study

Three students from the French University's Pharmacy program are going to France for further study, Xu Zhangfu, Sun Yun, and Wang Shaoding. They are scheduled to leave for France today (the 14th). The school's alumni association held a farewell banquet for them yesterday (the 13th) at the Zhimeilou Restaurant on Simalu Road, with more than 30 people including Zhu Wenxin attending. They dispersed after 10 pm. It is heard that Mr. Xu and others plan to enter the University of Lyon to specialize in pharmacy, which will take four years.

Heavy Selling Pressure on American Cotton

Yesterday, the American cotton market opened with bad news from Liverpool. The Liverpool gang sold off, the bulls closed out, and the cotton farmers hedged. Each month fell by 4 to 6 pounds per sound. Then the industry bought in when it fell, and it stabilized slightly. However, the selling pressure was very heavy, and the buyers mainly relied on the weak silver price. News from Washington said that Agriculture Minister Wallace may agree to stop the new cotton management plan until a large amount of production causes a large surplus. The market price fell by one point. After that, the cooperative sold off, and the market price became more tired. When the market closed, some shorts were covered, and it was slightly stable. It is estimated that the spot price fell by 4 pounds per sound, and the futures price fell by 4 to 16 pounds per sound. The British cotton spot price fell by 6 points, and the futures price fell by 3 to 5 points. Indian cotton rose due to reports that the Aumla cotton area continued to have wind and rain, and European exporters bought Aumla. Later, it fell back due to bad news from Liverpool. It is estimated that Pingor fell by 0.25 rupees, Aumla did not move, and Bairachi fell by 1.5 rupees. The original telegram is recorded on the left. (Telegram on the 12th)

According to the Mumbai telegram, the forecast for the opening on the 13th was Bairachi at 217 rupees, up 0.25, Aumla at 198 rupees, up 0.25 rupees, and Pingor at 158 rupees, unchanged.

Piece Goods: Cotton Cloth Factory's Futures Plate is Looser

Yesterday, the cloth market was firm because the cotton markets at home and abroad saw mixed ups and downs, the domestic spot yarn and flowers rose step by step, and the sales volume of spot yarn was considerable, causing the cloth price to remain solid. The factory's recent futures attitude is firm because there are still huge amounts of orders that have not been cleared, and the amount of goods is insufficient. However, the factory's futures plate is looser for the long-term futures because customers are not very interested in entering. The output of each factory is mostly fine twill and fine cloth. Yesterday, the spot fine cloth and grey fine twill were sold out due to the fact that the daily factory strike had a solution. The people who held the spot goods returned their minds and loosened, and the selling price fell back (per piece) by 5 points. The stack of goods is still sold at the original plate. The heavy-weight coarse cloth market of this factory is sluggish, but the light-weight coarse cloth and the fine cloth and fine twill of this factory are still good because of the lack of output. Yesterday, the demand from Hankou, Changsha, Hengzhou and other gangs along the Yangtze River was still good. They handled 100 pieces of spot fine twill, fine cloth, flannel, straight tribute, billie, and other goods. The Guangdong and Yunnan gangs entered more than 400 pieces of this month and December fine twill, straight tribute, billie, silk crepe de chine, printed poplin, straight tribute, etc. However, the actual needs of most customer gangs still lack a turnaround. The stock of each factory's printed straight tribute, billie, silk crepe de chine, and so on is getting thicker and there is no way out. The price of grey cloth is very expensive.

Metals: Prices Rising for All Goods

Prices for all metal goods, including black and white iron, as well as copper, lead, and tin, are on the rise. This is due to foreign factories reducing production (mainly to manufacture munitions), leading to numerous order delays. Business in this port city is booming, causing shortages in various markets, and thus prices are only rising, not falling. For example, refined lead has skyrocketed by three to four yuan, selling for 29 yuan. Block tin has risen by over ten yuan, selling for 194-195 yuan for the Xiao Heng brand and 214-215 yuan for the Dutch brand. Copper sheet prices have jumped from 55-56 yuan to 61-62 yuan, marking a significant increase. Other goods, such as white lead sheet, have risen by four to five yuan, selling for 155 yuan. Steel plates have increased by one yuan and a half, selling for twelve yuan. The market price for bamboo steel bars has also increased from 124-125 yuan to 130 yuan. However, the trading of the aforementioned goods is very active. Other items such as raw silk, angle iron, silver dollars, road leather, and lead wire are also reportedly on the rise.

Naaisi

Finance - Gold Price Declines with Pure Gold

The gold market was slightly sluggish yesterday due to forced swaps and the decline in pure gold. Trading fluctuated throughout the day. Major players’ supply and demand were mixed, but most limited their trading, resulting in limited price movement. In the morning, overseas silver markets experienced a two-day squeeze. Both British and American markets contracted. It was said that after closing, Indian bids reached 20 9375 pence, while sellers still demanded 21 pence, with few transactions. The forward silver price in Mumbai fell by 2.65 to 2.93 percent. Exchange rates opened flat and then contracted. London spot gold fell by 1.5 pence. The Central Bank's posted rates were flat for both British and American currencies. Customs gold unit fell by 3 percent. The standard gold bar price was posted at $1158.80, and pre-market trading opened lower at $54.00. While Da De Cheng was buying, Heng Yu was selling, retreating to within $4. The morning opened with lower prices. After the opening, major players jointly sold bars, and short sellers took the opportunity to increase their positions, leading to further declines. Long positions maintained support at lower prices, and spot dealers also bought. However, prices were soon pulled up, but due to continued short selling, although HSBC's posted rates for British and American currencies were flat, there was still a slight decline. Later, buying interest gradually increased, and although the silver balancing tax was down by $0.1175, it gradually rebounded. However, the market was quite stable, and the afternoon was even quieter. Although major players' supply and demand were still active, both sides were limited in their trading, resulting in fluctuations. The day's market conditions are recorded below.

The morning opening was $1153.50, down $0.60 from the previous close. Qia Feng Yong advanced to $4, but Da De Cheng and Da Jin Feng Yong immediately retreated to $3.30 after selling. Da De Cheng, Qia Feng Yong, Tong Feng, and Heng took advantage of the low prices to advance to $4. Jin Feng Yong and Da De Cheng were quite aggressive in selling. Although HSBC's posted rates for British and American currencies were flat, they still fell to $3.50. Cheng Da, Da De Cheng, Yuan Mao Yong, Tong Fu, and Qia Feng Yong successively bought in. Although the silver balancing tax was down by $0.1175, it gradually rebounded to $4. Qing, Yong Chun Yuan, and Yong limited their bar supply. The afternoon close was $1153.90.

The afternoon market opened at $1153.70, but Yu Yuan Mao Yong sold down to $1.60. Niu Yuan Yong and Yuan Mao Yong came in, rising to $3.80. Tong Tai Chang sold heavily. Although Fu Yu and others bought in, the closing was still $1153.50.

The closing price, according to the Central Bank's standard gold bar posting, was lowered to $1158.80. Based on the closing price, the net price was over $5. The registration for this month was $1151, and for December it was $1154. The morning water compensation was $1151. Red gold was increased by $6, to $1159.90. The spot market was even more stable. Refined red gold was increased by $14.50, with 70 taels sold by Tong Feng Heng. The buying price was increased by $10. Tianjin goods were increased by $10.25, but there were no transactions. The forecast for this swap session was strongly in favor of the long positions, with a premium of $2.50.

Trading within the exchange was mediocre. In summary, Tong, Heng, Qia Feng Yong, Tong Fu, Wan Xing, Sheng Yuan Yong, Yuan Mao Yong, Qian Chang, Xiang, etc., were on the buying side. Jin Feng Yong, Chun Yuan Yong, Qing Fa Yong, Yi Da Fu, Da Tong Tai Chang, etc., were on the selling side. Tong Feng Heng, Qia Feng Yong, and Yuan Mao Yong bought in first and then sold. Da De Cheng, Shen Da, Yong Heng Yu sold first and then bought.

The day's market was flat and sluggish, opening in the morning at $1153.90 and closing at $1153.50. The highest was $1154, and the lowest was $1153.30, with a fluctuation of $0.70. The result was a decrease of $1 from the previous close. There were still 7 bars remaining for this month. The December positions totaled 6986 bars, with 30 long positions and 32 short positions. The total number of transactions for the day was 1204 bars in the morning session and 714 bars in the afternoon session.

Swap Settles - Exchange Market Near Flat and Slightly Firm

The exchange market yesterday saw swap settlements, with near flat and slightly loose conditions. Chinese merchants remained active. In the morning, foreign cables indicated a two-day settlement, with both near and far London rates contracting by 1.125 pence. It was said that after closing, Indian bids reached 20.9375 pence, while sellers demanded 11 pence, with few transactions. The New York silver market contracted by 2 cents. The forward silver price in Mumbai fell by 2.65 to 2.93 percent. London spot gold fell by 1.5 pence. British to American rates remained unchanged. British to French rates fell by 3 pounds. American to British rates contracted by 0.4375. American to French rates fell by a small fraction. The Central Bank's posted rates were flat for both British and American currencies. Customs gold unit fell by 3 percent. The exchange market opened in the morning with the selling price for near-term British exchange at 1 shilling 2.5625 pence and American exchange at $29.625, slightly tighter than the previous close for both. After the opening, banks' activity was mixed. HSBC's posted rates were flat and stable. After entering the market, the silver balancing tax was announced, down by $0.1175, but banks' appetite remained healthy. The process was flat. In the afternoon, banks were buying American and selling British currencies. Chinese merchants were slightly buying forward shillings. The process was slightly flat. The closing selling price for near-term British exchange was a strong 1 shilling 2.5625 pence and American exchange at $29.625, flat for British and slightly tighter for American compared to the previous close, due to swap settlements. Forward rates were generally firm around 0.0625. Chinese merchants were actively selling $200,000 in American dollars, and shillings went from selling to buying. The transactions are recorded below.

British exchange opened in the morning with the selling price for near-term exchange at 1 shilling 2.5625 pence. Citibank sold to Mitsui for December at 5625. Netherlands bought November at 6875. Shanghai bought December at 625. The afternoon close for the selling price of near-term exchange was $29.625. In the afternoon, Citibank bought March at 4375. Silk and Tea - Japanese and American Silk Prices Rise for Consecutive Days - Silk Merchants Follow with a Price Increase of $15 - Trading Also Quite Active

Yesterday, overseas silk markets continued their strong rise. It was said that there was a labor strike among seamen in New York, and the arrival of raw silk was temporarily delayed. Spot goods became even scarcer, and only existing silk products were available. The silk price increased accordingly. Japanese silk 83 and 75 grades each rose by 3 cents per pound. Chinese silk rose by 2 cents each. Near-term standard silk rose by 3 cents, and long-term silk rose by 1 cent. Yokohama spot prices rose by $15, and futures rose by $13. The local silk market in Shanghai was quite active due to the increase in prices in Japan and the United States. Merchants followed suit with a price increase of approximately $15. For example, the 78 grade was sold yesterday at $760, an increase of $20 from before. Yesterday, foreign firms' appetite for buying remained strong. Firms such as Jardine Matheson had considerable transactions. User silk also became popular, and sales were strong. Lu factories, which had been silent for a long time, also became active yesterday. A total of 463 bales were sold citywide.

Green Tea (Lou Zhuang Zhen Mei) Trading is Quiet

Yesterday, the green tea market for foreign firms remained quiet. European firms indicated that foreign cables showed that the prices for Zhen Mei were too tight, making negotiations difficult. Items such as Needle Eyebrow (Zhen Mei) and Show Eyebrow (Xiu Mei) were in relatively strong demand, but inventories were lacking, and demand exceeded supply, leading to a wait-and-see attitude. Only firms such as Xie He and Jin Long bought over 200 cases of Zhen Mei green tea citywide, with prices ranging from $50 to $56, with little change from before.

Family Construction

— Wei Jing

A nation indeed needs construction, and so does a family. The responsibility for family construction undoubtedly falls more heavily on the shoulders of women. Therefore, I would like to bring this issue up for discussion.

Family construction can be divided into two major parts: material construction and spiritual construction.

Material construction can be divided into the following items:

* The tidiness of the home, such as the proper placement of all objects and furniture, making it aesthetically pleasing.

* Cleanliness and hygiene, such as regularly dusting and sweeping floors and windows. Regularly washing and disinfecting clothes and bedding. Food and drinks must be thoroughly steamed and cooked. Sour, rotten, or unclean items should be absolutely discarded. During seasons when epidemics occur, such as the prevalence of smallpox, cholera, malaria, and typhoid fever, efforts must be made to prevent the occurrence or spread of infectious diseases.

* Establishing a budget to reduce unnecessary expenses.

* Striving for savings to establish a solid foundation for the family's economic stability.

* Promoting exercise and noble entertainment, such as walking in the park, traveling to the countryside. Playing ball, such as tennis or table tennis. Visiting model families, holding family tea parties to exchange knowledge or opinions, subscribing to beneficial books and newspapers to increase knowledge, and playing musical instruments such as zithers.

* Promoting home industry, such as weaving, knitting, and children's bamboo and woodworking.

Spiritual construction can be divided into the following items:

* Creating an atmosphere of tranquility in the home, such as not speaking loudly intentionally. Placing objects gently, not carelessly. Children not knocking on tables and desks. Avoiding sudden running sounds.

* Creating an atmosphere of harmony in the home. All issues between husband and wife should be absolutely open and handled with mutual understanding and forgiveness. Treat children with patient guidance, never striking or scolding them. Treat servants with kindness and gentleness, not with harsh words or expressions.

* Cultivating good habits of tidiness, cleanliness, and exercise.

* Cultivating compassion and mutual aid, but not involving superstition.

* Cultivating a spirit of adventure and courage, but not wildness or recklessness. At the same time, patience must be trained, but absolutely not cowardice. Special attention must be paid when training children.

* Cultivating habits of frugality, but not to the point of stinginess.

* Cultivating a love of diligence. In particular, children must be made to perform domestic service for a certain amount of time each day to cultivate habits of diligence and responsibility.

* Speaking must be frank and honest, without lying, concealing, or making meaningless jokes. Display dignity within gentleness.

* Refrain from extravagance in tobacco, alcohol, cosmetics, and unnecessary sweets and food. All household items must be made, as much as possible, of domestic goods.

Individuals living in families that meet the standards of both material and spiritual well-being will undoubtedly be outstanding members of society. Furthermore, children trained in such families will undoubtedly be superior little citizens of the nation. However, unproductive citizens are useless and harmful to the nation and its people. To create excellent citizens capable of carrying forward and expanding the nation's glory, we must first start by working hard on family construction. May the housewives of the nation rise up and work directly on family construction, and indirectly promote the construction of society and the nation.

A Female Hero Against the Enemy

— Fan Xianwei

In the 52nd year before the Republic, Gengshen year, the sixth year of Emperor Xianfeng of the Qing Dynasty, the Anglo-French allied forces invaded Tianjin, directly threatening Beijing, burning the Old Summer Palace. Emperor Wenzong sought refuge in Rehe. The situation was dire. Fortunately, the Russian envoy Ignatiev mediated and negotiated the Treaty of Beijing. Our Kowloon Peninsula was ceded to Britain in this war, with countless losses in terms of ports opened and indemnities paid. At that time, the Chinese army relied on soldiers armed with swords and rattan shields to defend our territory. As for military weapons, we only had muzzle-loading guns! Of course, we couldn't compete with their giant ships carrying cannons weighing thousands of tons. But at that time, there was a female hero near the Old Summer Palace who witnessed the increasing foreign aggression and the imminent crisis of the nation. She raised the banner of rebellion, bravely resisting the enemy. Unfortunately, she was outnumbered and ultimately defeated. But as a weak woman who could bravely defend against the strong enemy, she is truly worthy of our admiration!

The female hero's name was Wan Zhen, surnamed Feng, originally from Shandong. She was 19 years old. Her father's name was Sanbao, skilled in martial arts. During the war of the allied forces, her family happened to live in Xiezhuang, ten miles away from the Old Summer Palace. Because she had been practicing martial arts with her father since she was a child, she was quite good at boxing. When the allied forces burned the Old Summer Palace, she did not want Xiezhuang to fall into the hands of the enemy. She gathered young people from the village, dressed in black and armed with white blades, to protect their homeland. They ambushed in the forest. Soon after, enemy cavalry arrived with cannons. She led the crowd, wielding knives and slashing fiercely, attacking them from both sides. They moved swiftly and bravely, mowing down everything in their path! The Western soldiers suffered a major defeat, abandoning their cannons and fleeing, with numerous deaths and injuries. Due to the overwhelming disparity in numbers, they had to retreat. This page of anti-enemy history may not be recorded in official history, so I specifically record it to encourage future generations.

Glorious Women

— Fang Lijun

Correspondence from Xikang

This is our Chinese society's fixed iron circle. From ancient times, it has been a male-centered society. Women are merely appendages of men. Therefore, there is fundamentally no place for women in Chinese society. This is an undeniable fact before us. However, when we look back at the women of Xikang and the current state of their society, we are surprised and find it hard to believe. Because the customs of Xikang are completely different from ours; in other words, it is exactly the opposite.

The state of Xikang society: men, apart from hunting and going to other places to do business, leave all other household chores and affairs to the full responsibility of women. Furthermore, even in the city's shops, the staff are exclusively women, working diligently. Because Xikang society is centered on women.

Because it is a female-centered society, it is the same as areas that are male-centered societies. In Xikang, polyandry is prevalent, opposing the polygamy system here. This may be due to the environment and traditional concepts.

They are open and free about social interactions between men and women; they do not have the constraints of old customs and feudalism. Regarding the relationship between the sexes, as long as both the man and woman agree, they can freely unite. Moreover, some women may not even have consulted their parents when they have fallen in love or have other relations with a man. They only inform them afterward, and then hold a simple and quick wedding ceremony.

As for the lives of women in rural Xikang? Their work is complex and busy. They are responsible for all the hard work, from sowing, fertilizing, to plowing, harvesting, and so on. In addition, many women also engage in animal husbandry. Apart from accompanying the herds of cattle and sheep to the mountains, they sometimes also have to take care of the cows and sheep in the pasture, and keep watch at night. From morning to night, they have no time to rest. Thus, if we compare the sisters of Xikang with the parasitic women in the crazy cities who apply powder and rouge, go to the cinema, go to dance halls, and are played with as toys by men, the difference between them is too great. The former are laborers who produce for society, while the latter are useless parasites.

So, let us say it frankly and happily: one has fulfilled the responsibility of being human, while the other is only for consumption and has no soul. They have simply lost their human form!

Their clothing varies depending on their economic status. The common people mostly wear cotton or woolen cloth. The aristocrats wear fine woolen cloth or Tibetan cloth imported from India. The style of their clothes is a round collar, long sleeves, from shoulder to ankle, with a floral belt tied around the waist, and a coat or shawl is worn on the outside. And the feudal poison that is most preserved in mainland China—breast binding, is considered a strange trend there; therefore, there is absolutely no trace of it.

Every New Year or festival is their happiest time. They invite many friends to join in the group celebration at night. They wear beautiful and delicate clothes, hold hands and dance, and sing. They also welcome men to join their group. They do not sleep until late at night.

The women of Xikang are glorious and worthy of praise.

The Life of Women on West Dongting Mountain

— Ya Fei

West Dongting Mountain is an isolated island in Taihu Lake, about 90 li by water from Suzhou. It is not only scenic, but also rich in products. Since the Taiping Rebellion, the mountain has rarely been affected by the situation, and even disasters and banditry have not been as severe as in other places. If it were not for the current rural bankruptcy, I think this place could be described as a paradise. But the education there is very backward, and the customs are very closed off, especially the lives of ordinary women, which are almost completely stuck in the eighteenth century. They are bound by the traditional concepts of feudal etiquette and are content to be slaves to men.

Almost 100% of the women here have not received an education. The thoughts of feudal etiquette govern their entire behavior, and the "three obediences and four virtues" dictate their entire lives. "At home, obey your mother; when married, obey your husband" is their unchanging women's virtue, and "strictly guard chastity and obey your husband" is the great righteousness that every woman should understand. Therefore, on West Dongting Mountain, a woman who remarries after her husband's death is looked down upon by everyone. Moreover, when she remarries, she must choose a time late at night, when no one is around, to get into the sedan chair or perform the ceremony. It must be done in a deserted temple or on ownerless land. If someone sees it or gets into the sedan chair on someone else's land, it is considered unlucky and they must "pay respects" and light incense. However, a man who loses his wife can remarry at any time, and no one will criticize him.

The worst thing is to be a widow waiting for a husband you've never met. Some of them are child brides, while others have never even met their fiancé. But once their fiancé dies, they actually have to live the life of a widow. I believe there are no women in the world more pitiful than these! In the past, many women were willing to build a reputation for themselves as chaste and virtuous women. Therefore, wherever you went, you would see many arches of chastity or arches of virtue. But what are they for now? I really can't understand.

When a new daughter-in-law marries into the family, she has to bring "good luck" to the family for three years. If, after she enters the house, any of the flowers, fruits, silkworms, or rice does not have a good harvest, it is said that she has a bad fate. If the husband or parents-in-law get sick, or even die, then she cannot escape the crime of being an "eight-failure life" or a "white tiger star"!

In the countryside, it is a glorious thing for a man to steal another man's wife, but on the contrary, if a woman commits adultery, she will encounter the seven grounds for divorce. However, if a husband abandons his wife, the wife has no choice but to work as a servant to make a living, and cannot remarry. Therefore, many women here commit suicide or seek a quick death because they cannot bear the torture of life, but few cases are ever fairly adjudicated by the law. Most of them are dealt with in a perfunctory manner. It is very common for parents-in-law to abuse or even beat their daughters-in-law. If the daughter-in-law happens to resist the parents-in-law, everyone will think it is an act of "great rebellion".

Although modern law has recognized women's right to inherit property, the women here not only do not enjoy the rights granted by law, but also all economic power is in the hands of men. Therefore, a woman in the process of being a daughter-in-law is just a servant who washes clothes, cooks meals, and works tirelessly, or a machine for giving birth to children, but the result is still not as good as the treatment of a servant, let alone any compensation.

They suffer from excessive childbirth and excessive fatigue, and if they get sick, they are not given treatment or medical care. This is especially common, but they think that a daughter-in-law is like foot-washing water, and they can marry another one if she dies. Moreover, there is a local saying that "it is a great misfortune for a wealthy family not to have their daughter-in-law die for three years", so they look down on daughters-in-law very much there.

In recent years, due to the impact of rural bankruptcy, they have also embarked on the road of working as servants in the city in order to survive. Therefore, it is easy to encounter women from West Dongting Mountain in Shanghai, Suzhou, Huzhou, and other places recently. This is really not a good phenomenon!

At present, there are ten county-run primary schools, one private high school, and four primary schools on the mountain. Girls also seem to have a little opportunity to receive education, but due to the poison of tradition, only one or two out of a hundred girls can actually have the opportunity to enter the school gate.

Finally, when it comes to marriage, both men and women have very little autonomy and are still subject to matchmaker's words and parents' orders, a set of buying and selling behaviors.

Now, the slogans and facts of women's liberation are erupting like sparks, and all the problems have been very seriously shown to us. But this torrent of the times has not yet washed over those remote rural villages.

I believe that this situation is a relief of the rural women in various places and it is definitely not only in a corner of Dongting West Mountain!

Holding Brooms to Sweep Away Bad Habits

Sewing Women

— Qi Feng

One of the Female Professions on the Streets

Although sewing women are a lowly occupation in the city, their widespread presence is often found among the proletariat. However, the sewing women mentioned here are completely different from the commonly known female tailors. Female tailors are hired to work in employers' homes, and their treatment includes meals in addition to their wages. Therefore, the lives of female tailors are completely opposite to those of sewing women. Sewing women not only have no meals provided but also receive pitifully low wages. They do not always have work available; sometimes, they have no work to do for an entire day. This forces them to find other ways to make a living (readers can surely understand what "finding other ways" means). As a result, they are seen as lowly women with lowly occupations.

Based on general observations, most of these sewing women are from Jiangbei. There are compelling reasons why they abandon their hometowns, endure hardships, and come to the bustling city to engage in this livelihood. Years of economic recession have bankrupted the rural economy. To make a living, many strong men leave the countryside and go to large cities to seek employment. However, their daily income is still insufficient to support their families. Therefore, middle-aged women have no choice but to wander into the city and join the common struggle. Due to limited knowledge and skills, besides scavenging and peddling, sewing becomes a field of their professions? It meets the need for clothing repairs for solitary, proletarian laborers living in foreign lands.

Of course, their lives are undoubtedly very hard. Every day, they come out of the slums and wander the streets, going door to door seeking employment. They scrape together their living expenses from this piecemeal labor. Undoubtedly, they can barely survive the unbearable hunger, and their suffering is imaginable.

In short, they are ten thousand times better than those social parasites who are incapable of production! We should sympathize with and praise them!

Special Feature of This Newspaper

An Interview with Ms. Bao Yahui

— Ping

One evening in late autumn, the reporter mingled with the audience exiting the Guotai Theater, feeling a bit dizzy. Suddenly, a thought crossed my mind: wasn't the residence of the female painter Bao Yahui just on Zuo Shan? Why not visit her along the way? Once the idea was decided, I set off for my destination with light steps. After finding the gate, I pressed the doorbell. A man resembling a doorman led me into the reception room to sit down.

After a while, Ms. Bao pushed the door open and came in, accompanied by a slender young man in a student uniform. After introductions, I learned that he was her nephew, Pan Guan Jun, a budding calligrapher who had recently been writing in the style of Han and Wei, known throughout the north and south. I had long heard of him and unexpectedly met him by chance. After some pleasantries, we sat around the round table and began to talk.

"Is Mr. Xulun at home? I was hoping to talk to you both about household economics today, as Mr. Pan is an accountant and likely has clear insights on this issue to provide a reference for families large and small."

"I'm sorry! He has a banquet tonight and has already left. Talking about household economics is indeed important, but unfortunately, I have no interest in it. Instead of making presumptuous remarks, would you mind if we chose another topic?"

"Then please, Ms., share your opinions."

She smiled, appearing very modest: "I can't think of anything to say for the moment. All I know is about painting."

"That's also good. Ms. is a painter, so please tell us about your successful journey in learning to paint."

"I can say that I have an interest in painting, but I can't speak of talent or skill, let alone success. However, my mother had considerable success in painting, and I was influenced by her from a young age, gradually developing an interest. I remember when I was receiving secondary education in my hometown, the school had several hours of drawing lessons each week. At that time, my enthusiasm was very high, and I was very bold, drawing whatever I saw and starting to copy landscapes. Once, at a performance exhibition, they selected my large-scale copy of Wang Lutai's 'Danlou Chunxiao,' hanging it in the center? It attracted the attention of viewers, and the county magistrate and school inspector came to visit. When they learned it was my work, they specially praised me, deeming me promising. My small heart was truly delighted, and I became even more motivated. However, there was a lack of teachers and friends to guide and learn from in the inland. After coming to Shanghai, I sought guidance from Mr. Lu Tieshi for many years and traveled to famous mountains and rivers, admiring many works by famous artists. My experience has broadened somewhat, but limited by my innate talent, I cannot make significant progress."

"A painter needs to be close to mountains and rivers, and the more experience they have, the grander their style. Have you been to Guilin, Yandang, Huangshan, etc.?"

"I'm very ashamed! I've always wanted to go to Guilin but haven't had the chance yet. I've been to Mount Tai, the Great Wall, Mount Chong, West and East Tianmu, and Yandang, but unfortunately, I encountered heavy rain and hid in the temple for two days without going out. I haven't even seen the Dalongqiu in Yandang, which I've always longed for, which is truly regrettable! People say that Huangshan is really wonderful, but the mountain is too steep, and my waist and legs are not strong enough, so I dare not dream of it. Landscape painting has a type of wrinkle technique, called 'Pi Ma wrinkles' and 'Axe Cut wrinkles.' I didn't understand it at first, but after seeing many Huangshan films and observing the stone patterns of the mountains, I realized that they were indeed the same as the painting methods."

At this point, the young painter spoke up: "Honestly speaking, the strangeness of the pines and rocks of Huangshan is truly captivating. I don't know about Yunnan and Guizhou, but as for the famous mountains of the Central Plains, this is certainly the best. I heard that Mount Hua is also like this, but I haven't been there. However, Huangshan also has considerable shortcomings, namely the lack of waterfalls. Jiulong Waterfall is the only one, but compared to the Dalongqiu of Yandang, it is a small witch compared to a great one."

The reporter took a sip of tea and glanced at a landscape painting of Huangshigu hanging on the right wall, which triggered the conversation: "I've heard people say that Chinese painting flourished in the Qing Dynasty, with numerous schools and factions. Among the many painters, who would you consider the representative of Qing painting?"

Ms. Bao hesitated slightly before saying: "That's hard to say. Generally speaking, it is naturally the Four Wangs (Wang Shimin, Wang Jian, Wang Yuanqi, Wang Lutai). Among the Four Wangs, Wang Yuanqi has the deepest attainment. We know that Chinese landscape painting is divided into Northern and Southern Schools. The Southern School is independent and innovative, while the Northern School was founded by Li Sixun. Although they do not use topography as a boundary, they are vastly different. Since Tang Yin of the Ming Dynasty combined the Northern style with the Southern style, everyone thought that the North and South would converge. In fact, this accomplishment was undoubtedly achieved by Wang Yuanqi alone. As for Wang Shimin and Wang Jian, they deliberately imitated Dong Qichang. Dong Qichang is naturally an outstanding figure of the Southern School, and the two lived at the same time, so they were very close to Dong Qichang. Wang Lutai's brushwork is skilled but not ingratiating, vivid but not rough, deeply capturing the essence of Huang Gongwang, which is not easy to achieve."

At this time, Pan Jun nodded frequently, so I asked: "Mr. Pan, what do you think of your aunt's high opinion?"

He took a big puff of his cigarette, and a puff of smoke rolled out with a smile: "Absolutely! Absolutely! However, I think Wu Yushan (Wu Li) surpassed both the North and the South with his majestic style. Although his fame at the time was not as great as Wang Yuanqi's and others, there were other reasons for this. Perhaps Wu Yushan had a bit of a celebrity air, arrogant by nature, unwilling to curry favor with his masters, so even in his old age, he was still wandering the world, with no intention of seeking fame. Not to mention anything else, we see very few of his paintings in traditional copies. In terms of his works, he can also be considered a representative master."

The conversation grew longer and longer, and the enthusiasm grew stronger and stronger. I quickly closed the conversation, shook hands, and said goodbye.

Ms. Yahui

Dinner Party

— Xue Ying

I once attended a dinner party, and the impression it left on us has not faded to this day, perhaps never will! On a Sunday in early autumn, I received an invitation from a classmate I had grown up with since childhood, inviting me to a dinner party at the newly opened Xinlu Grand Hotel. Dinner parties are very ordinary, but that day, because I hadn't been in touch with this classmate for a long time, I couldn't help but feel a little surprised. I first called the Daxin Bank, intending only to ask for the telephone number of their president, Li, but the operator unexpectedly told me that President Li was currently at the bank, so I spoke directly with Li Ruifu. I couldn't help but ask him why he was still at the bank on Sunday. He said he was very busy. I said that since he was so busy, why did he still want to invite guests? He said it wasn't an invitation, just a chat with a few old friends. I asked who else was coming. He said that Zhao Shu and his wife would probably be there. After saying that, he hung up the phone. I thought that this President Li was too presumptuous. When someone called him, he didn't even say, "Please be sure to come tonight." But I didn't want to argue with him, and I had a special reason for wanting to see Zhao Shu's wife. That evening, I arrived at the new restaurant on time. I asked, but the host hadn't arrived yet, but the waiter said that President Li had booked a room and paid ten dollars in advance, and said that if he didn't come, he would ask the guest to dine alone. At that time, I was really hungry, so I sat alone in that empty room, facing the three empty chairs, and ate a fine dinner.

After returning home, I felt like I had a huge, unresolved puzzle in my heart. I couldn't figure out what Li Ruifu was up to. The next morning, I unexpectedly saw a shocking piece of bad news in the local news of various newspapers, titled "President Li Ruifu of Daxin Bank Drove into the River," roughly saying that around 7 o'clock last night, Li Ruifu was driving his own car, traveling near a certain pier in Yangshupu, when he accidentally crashed into the Huangpu River. Zhao Shu and his wife, the head of the remittance department of Daxin Bank, were also in the car, and all three drowned. Their bodies had not yet been recovered. At first, I was naturally very sad, but later, after thinking carefully, I felt very surprised because Li Ruifu and Zhao Shu's homes were clearly near Haig Road in West Shanghai, and the Daxin Bank was also located on Hankou Road. They had no need to go to Yangshupu at all, and around 7 o'clock was the time of the dinner party that Li Ruifu had arranged. Why didn't he come to the Xinlu Grand Hotel on Xizang Road and instead went to Yangshupu? It was too strange!

At noon that day, a registered letter from Li Ruifu was suddenly delivered to my house. How could a dead person still send a letter? I rushed to look at the postmark, and it turned out it was sent yesterday. I hurriedly opened it and saw that it was indeed his suicide note. He said that he invited me to dinner, but he didn't necessarily want me to go, as long as I knew that he had done this. So he didn't strongly invite me on the phone, and he was writing this letter to me when I called him. He told me that he deeply regretted being frivolous in school and having a love affair with Zou Xian ＋ Zhao Shu's wife — and having a physical relationship. But he was already married and couldn't find a way, so he tried his best to introduce her to Zhao Shu, and after their marriage, he spared no effort to recommend Zhao Shu to Daxin Bank, where he served as the head of the remittance department. Unexpectedly, Zhao Shu gradually learned about the relationship between his wife and Li Ruifu, and his attitude became very overbearing. Within three years, he had embezzled several times, and Li Ruifu was forced to make up for it. Recently, he speculated unsuccessfully and lost more than 200,000 yuan at once. Li Ruifu was worried about being sued by the board of directors on the one hand, and Zhao Shu was forcing him to declare bankruptcy and compensate for him on the other. He felt that he had been very unfair to his wife and children in the past, so he decided to preserve his family property and was willing to take Zhao Shu and his wife with him to the bottom of the river.

Now, two years have passed, and I have followed his instructions and tried my best to take care of his family, but his wife and children still don't know that he committed suicide!

Being Too Fat

No. 88, Student Huai Shen of Daxia University asked: (1) My body is too fat; although I often do indoor exercises, I still don't see any weight loss? (2) How to practice contraception? (3) I get headaches when reading for too long, my memory is poor, is it effective to take Ai Luo Brain Tonic? (4) Does eating cod liver oil make people fatter?

Answer: (1) A person's body fat or thinness is determined by the amount of fat stored in the body, so if you plan to lose weight, you must remove the fat in the body. Reducing fat is called lipolysis. And almost everything a person eats in a day has the potential to turn into fat. So, to lose weight, you can only reduce food and increase exercise. The former can reduce the production of fat, and the latter can increase the consumption of fat. In nutrition, the production and sales of fat are calculated in "Caville" units, which is the same as calculating heat in physics. Although the amount of "calories" used by each person to maintain nutrition varies, it is generally between 5,000 and 7,000. So, after calculating the calories input into the body every day, if you reduce it below the amount of consumption, the fat in the body will gradually decrease, which means that the person will slowly lose weight. On this point, Mr. Shen can buy a book with a table of food calorie estimates, and calculate his diet according to this book. (2) Not within the scope of the answer, sorry I cannot answer. (3) For neurasthenia, please inject "Blusen". (4) Yes. It can make people fat.

Shepherd's Purse

— Liao Chuxiu

Mr. Zhou Zuoren once described shepherd's purse in his "Wild Vegetables of My Hometown" as follows: "...Shepherd's purse is a wild vegetable that people in eastern Zhejiang often eat in spring. Not to mention the countryside, even in the city, as long as there are families with back gardens, they can pick and eat it at any time. Women and children, each with a pair of scissors and a "seedling basket," squat on the ground searching, which is an interesting game and work. At that time, the children sang: "Shepherd's purse and toothed grass, sister married at the back door." Later, toothed grass was brought into the city for sale by villagers, but shepherd's purse is still a kind of wild vegetable, which must be picked by oneself."

The people in my hometown are poorer than those in eastern Zhejiang. They search for anything that can be sold for money and sell it. Therefore, some people also carry shepherd's purse to the streets for sale.

Shepherd's purse is really a wild vegetable that grows everywhere. Like in my family, there is a small back garden, so there is no need to take it from elsewhere. In spring, the afternoons are really long and a little scary, so my mother would take us to the back garden to stroll around. On the one hand, she would call the little maid to "pick" shepherd's purse. Picking shepherd's purse is called "picking" in our hometown, just like in eastern Zhejiang. However, instead of scissors, we use a special triangular knife for digging grass for feeding sheep. We don't necessarily eat it after picking it. Often, it turns yellow and cannot be eaten, so we throw it away. However, my mother always asked the little maid to "pick" it every other day, completely as a pastime.

In spring, when the shepherd's purse is in bloom, I would run to the back garden to pick it every day. At the same time, I would sing an incomplete children's song that I had heard:

"Shepherd's purse flowers bloom layer by layer like a pearl tower, rapeseed flowers bloom like gold—"

One afternoon passed in this song.

Jiang Wu Niu Xiu's "Early Grass" says: "In lean years, the sweet grass comes first." Sweet grass is shepherd's purse. Liu Bowen's early spring poem: "Happy to see children reporting each other, shepherd's purse coming up by the wall." I don't know if it's true? But shepherd's purse grows very early, and it is especially delicious in early spring because it is tender. Shepherd's purse is always a new dish in New Year's cuisine.

Gu Lu's "Qing Jia Yin" says in "March Wild Vegetable Flowers": "Shepherd's purse flowers are commonly called wild vegetable flowers because there is a saying that on the third day of the third month, ants climb onto the stove mountain. On the third day, families put vegetable flowers on the stove to suppress insects and ants. Village children shout and sell them endlessly, or women wear them in their hair to pray for clear eyes, commonly known as 'eye-brightening flowers,' or they are fried with last year's rice cakes and eaten, saying they can brighten the eyes, called 'eye-brightening cakes.'" Su Dongpo's "Mutual Induction of Things" also says: "On the third day of the third month, collect shepherd's purse flowers and place them on lampstands, so that moths and mosquitoes will not fly over." This is naturally not true. Even the people of Wu now put shepherd's purse flowers on the stove on the third day of the third month, but it is only because they have been doing so throughout history.

You Rucheng's "West Lake Tour Guide" says: "On the third day of the third month, men and women all wear shepherd's purse flowers. There is a saying: "Wearing shepherd's purse in spring, peach and plum blossoms are ashamed of their beauty." Wu Manyun's "Jiangxiang Seasonal Objects" preface: "In Hangzhou customs, on the Shangsi Festival, shepherd's purse flowers are placed on the stove to drive away insects and ants. The poem says, 'A branch of spring is picked towards the stove corner.'" Hangzhou and Suzhou are not far apart, and customs have their similarities, but Hangzhou is especially fond of shepherd's purse because of the two proverbs.

"Qing Jia Lu" records that the people of Wu stir-fry shepherd's purse with last year's rice cakes. Mr. Zhou Zuoren also said: "But people in eastern Zhejiang don't pay much attention to these things. They just pick it to make dishes or stir-fry rice cakes." Shepherd's purse itself is very delicious, and because it is a "wild vegetable," it is always mainly vegetarian. Stir-frying with meat or chicken is also very good, but it always feels inappropriate. But in Shanghai, people probably only eat it stir-fried with meat or chicken.

It has been ten years since I followed my mother to watch her pick shepherd's purse. It has also been four or five years since I saw the "pearl tower" like shepherd's purse flowers. My hometown is even poorer, and people naturally eat more wild shepherd's purse. I don't know if there is as much shepherd's purse in my family's back garden in recent years as there used to be? If the saying "In lean years, the sweet grass comes first" is correct, then there must be very little. Only the two incomplete children's songs that I heard are still not forgotten:

"Shepherd's purse flowers bloom layer by layer like a pearl tower, rapeseed flowers bloom like gold!"

Rural Life

— Huang

The Melon Trellis in the Pond

I went for a leisurely stroll in the suburbs.

The scenery in the suburbs seems unchanged, but the smoke from the thatched huts has become faint and weak. The pond in my memory, under the quiet autumn sun, rippled with silver, and the ducks floated freely.

There is a melon trellis in the pond, with slender loofah vines creeping beside it. The tender yellow flowers, like their owner, open their starved mouths. Two or three malnourished loofahs hang down, with manure baskets underneath to catch them. Manure basket, you filthy thing, you are precisely the cradle of new life!

Bloodstains on the Roadside

A sharp gunshot jolted me awake from my dream. I hurriedly got out of bed and saw my younger brother's sorrowful face. He was trembling all over, speaking slowly and weakly.

"Brother, three people were shot dead outside the back door." The back door faces the highway. Just then, a burst of noisy voices came, mixed with the hoarse cries of several women.

"My son...!"

"You died so miserably...!"

I sat blankly on the edge of the bed, listening to the mournful cries, imagining the bloodstains flying and splashing on the roadside, on the green grass. I vaguely saw a young woman holding a male corpse and weeping bitterly, perhaps her father, perhaps her husband! Perhaps her younger brother.

A string of tears streamed down my cheeks.

In my hallucination, the purple blood gradually, gradually expanded, occupying all the space before my eyes, gradually closing in on me.

Until I came to my senses, the cries outside faded away. I hurriedly walked to the wall, stood on the table, and opened the window in the back. The sandy ground outside was stained with several patches of crimson blood. The corpses were gone, but the footprints treading on the blood stretched into the distance.

"Dead, may you rest in peace—someone has stepped over your bloodstains and gone ahead!"

Sea

My hometown is by the sea. I remember when I was a child, we held hands with our companions, walked on the fine sand, and wandered along the seashore. We picked up seashells and dug sand pits. When we were tired, we sat blankly, gazing at the boundless sea before us. At that time, the sea was like our mother, caressing us.

But now I have returned to my hometown, and I cannot see my loving mother. The sea has also lost its gentle maternal nature.

I walked to the seaside alone, at dusk. In the distance, the rolling mountains connected with the evening mist, and the high tide sea was like an angry tyrant. It tossed and turned, roaring.

Under the twilight, the sea's angry posture was magnificent, yet terrifying. It was like someone who had just broken free from chains, it rebelled.

The beloved hometown, the affectionate sea, only remain in my memory. What changed them? What changed them?

I looked at the sea, but it did not answer me, instead, it responded with roars and incessant churning.

Beauty and Hero

Young Zhou Daozun and Feng Tiren both love the young woman Sun Liying. As a result, Daozun succeeds and Tiren fails. During a war against a foreign country, Tiren resolutely joins the front lines and is injured.

After marriage, Liying and Daozun learn of this news and go to see him, deeply moved. They understand "Country Before Family"! So Daozun also follows the troops going to the front to fight, and Liying stays in the rear to serve in the hospital...

Movies

Grand Light Screens "The Battle Between Spirit and Flesh"

Starring Warner Baxter and Myrna Loy

"The Battle Between Spirit and Flesh一To　Mory－with　Love," starring Warner Baxter and Myrna Loy, is the latest production from 20th Century Fox. This film can be divided into two aspects: One aspect is about how a tender life and feelings between husband and wife can endure and not be broken by any misunderstanding; the other is about how a man who admires a beautiful woman in his heart sees her marry another man, and that man is his best friend. Infinite pain is hidden in his heart, and in the end, he sacrifices himself to fulfill the happiness of others. Warner Baxter and Myrna Loy play a young couple, sometimes embracing and cuddling, sometimes arguing, performing vividly. Ian Hunter plays another man, deep and experienced, and his acting skills are even more amazing. The film is scheduled to be released in Grand Light starting today.
